O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh ye, most dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last part of the knowledge of medicine together with its contents, and I have finished it through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in vision that I have completed it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and lost everywhere, so is the science destroyed and demolished, and nothing remains from it except the small descriptions in books of the ancients that were moved by hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this has come the error and vanity, and the intentions have been closed and the science has been estranged.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I should revive it together with the ordering of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come along with the forms of the cauteries' instruments and of the other tools of the craft with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, such as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because of this reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has been estranged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who undertakes this to ascend in the knowledge of anatomy, as Galen says, as long as he knows the joints of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and tendons and the number of them, and their movements and restings, and from where their issue comes.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because of this says Hippocrates that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little, and likewise in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	And we tell you in the introduction of this book that who is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned, let him guard himself lest he err and deceive men; thus I have wanted many times to warn those who undertake this science but abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a foolish surgeon who cut, that is, an abscess or boil on the neck of a woman, and he cut the arteries of the neck; why so much blood issued forth that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I have seen another surgeon who treated an old man's stone, and the stone was great; so he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if it were cut out, he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I have seen another surgeon who took on the care of a duke from our land, who had a broken leg and with the break was wounded. And the ignorant surgeon bound the break over the wound with tight ligatures, and did not let it be washed at all, and thus left it like that for a long time; and he forbade anyone to untie them, and so remained until the leg became gangrenous and came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come to loosen the leg; and when I loosened it, he was at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But the corruption was already confirmed in the member, and I could not heal it, and the corruption did not cease to progress through the member until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I have seen another surgeon who burst an infected abscess, and then it inflamed because of the wickedness of his treatment.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For when a cancer is purged of melancholic humor, it does not agree to be touched with iron unless in such a place where one can entirely remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the art of surgery is divided into two sections: one where there is danger in many situations; and I will show you in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Why it is necessary that you take care of yourselves so that the foolish mouth cannot speak evil of you. If you take up your arms in defense, and approach your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that through the grace of God you come to salvation and are praised; and leave the frightful diseases with grievous consequences; and take away from yourselves those things that cause doubt, and have courage in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	The Galen says in some of his warnings: "Do not take on a sick patient unless you are called foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have compiled this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about cauterization with fire and medical cautery, and it is the chapter ordered from head to foot; and of the forms of instruments, and of cauterizing iron, and of all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and venesection and wounds, and extracting arrows, and similar things; and it is the chapter that orders and describes the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and fractures, and similar things; and it is ordered from head to foot, and describes the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, so that we may remember the work, it is necessary for me to say the quality of each aid and the harm of each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of each aid and the harm is the longest word and most subtle science and secret response; and many of the wise have spoken about it and agreed with it; and I will shorten their words because I fear length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization aids universally to all temperaments where there is matter, except for two temperaments: namely, the hot temperament with excess of matter, and the dry temperament with excess of matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the hot and dry temperament with excess of matter, one group said that cauterization is a great aid, and the other group said the opposite, that cauterization is not useful for diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be treated with heat or dryness, nor is it suitable for treating hot and dry diseases; and those who say the opposite claim that cauterization does great aid in treating hot and dry diseases that come into the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you consider the body of man and its moisture compared to the temperament of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this saying.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, do not interfere with it unless you are the one who has tried it and know by long experience the chapter of cauterization, and the diversity of temperaments of men, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the remedies and the time of application; for as to other complexions, we have no fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the surgeons assembled and agreed on cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cauterization with fire is one of the secrets of treatments, and of greater goodness than medical cauterization.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not affect any member except the one that is burned, and it does no harm to another member if its name is known.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The hot medicines pass from member to member in scattering, and bring grievous diseases to the member; and it is possible that they kill the patient. The fires due to their greatness and the goodness of their substance do not cause these things, if there is no superfluity.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this by experiment and through the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things; and for this reason I excuse myself for the length of my words, because I do not like to deprive you of the secret which fire holds, and the quality of the work, how it heals diseases in bodies, as the philosophers say in demonstrating; take it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on the time when cauterizations should be done and chose specific hours.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is advisable in all times, because the remedies provided by cauterization are placed under, and especially when cauterizations are for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait until a greater evil comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, as foolish surgeons do; for the disease that is healed by cauterization does not recur, and they say so themselves. But it's not like they believe, because cauterizations are not just a medicine that changes the temperament, but also dry up the humors that cause pain, and are more valuable than other medicines in terms of speed, effectiveness, and the virtue of their work and their treatment.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is a possible thing that the disease comes back once, according to the temperament of the patient and the place and virtue of the disease, and excesses are gathered in him from the consumption of foods and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered at a place where there is little excess and moisture, such as for dens pain with cauterizations, and similar things, and that pain does not recur; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and it is true; but they do not believe that cauterization is worth trying after other treatments, but their intentions are false, and cauterization is the last resort of medicine because when we administer other modes of treatment for a disease and they do not work, then we administer the cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is clear that cauterizations are the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish surgeons.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterizations made with a golden instrument are more effective than those made with iron, and they did not say this only because of the quality of gold and its high substance; and they said that the place where the cauterization is made does not cause corruption, but this is not true for I have tried it and found that it is true in some men; and a golden cauterization is more effective than an iron one, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And in any case, when you heat an instrument made of gold, you cannot tell if it is hot enough by its color, and it cools down quickly; and if you heat it too much, it becomes damaged; and thus there are enough obstacles.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use cauterizations made of iron that we have made suitable for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have arranged this chapter from head to foot, so that the way is more easy to find.
dou cautere olivaire	From cauterization of olive oil.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cauterization is useful for moisture and coldness on the brain, and there are two types made by the cause of a disease called "soda", and by the cause of many humors that descend from the head to the ears, and for a multitude of dreams and pain in the temples and throat, and especially for all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cauterization is that the patient should be purged by a medicinal solution that cleanses the head three or four times, according to what virtue and age and custom of the patient can tolerate; and then reheat the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and put his hands on the scale; after putting the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and let where blood will come from it, then heat up the cauterization called "olivare", which is in this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it on the marked spot with ink, and make a descending and spreading motion with your hand little by little, turning it over; then lift up your hand suddenly, and reward the place if you see the bone 1 small inch deep; and if you don't see it, repeat the cauterization until you see the bone as I told you; after taking 1 piece of thread, put it in a warm wet cotton swab inside, and put it on the spot, and leave it for 3 days; then put on moistened cloth wrapped in a cloth; and leave it there until the heat is gone; then heal the wound with ointment called "tetrafarmacium" until it's healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges itself; and for this reason, it is more helpful.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that the cauterization should be done in such a way that part of the bone is burned, and then the burned part of the bone is to be removed and healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the others say that the cauterization should be done so deeply that it reaches as far down into the bone as a thread that women put in their looms, and that the wound should be left open for a long time to let the humors drain out; then it should be cured and closed.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to me to be entirely good in all cases, except perhaps for men who are already weak; and I think that I should leave it alone, because the nerves are weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we have seen in other members; and similarly, if the patient's nerve is weak by nature, the initial effect of cauterization may be more salutary and less risky for me, and that is what I use to ensure a safe outcome.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From the ancient pain in the head.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When a chronic pain comes to the head and lasts for a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie", and purges of the head and oils and plasters; and if one does the cauterization that we have just mentioned, it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take note if the nerve of the patient is strong and not too cold; then apply a cauterization under that one which we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Then do the cauterization on each horn of the head right up to the bone, as we have said before, and do one cauterization in the place called "vasselz"; and it is a spot where you apply cupping glasses; and lift your hand so that you don't see right up to the bone: the patient feels a much greater pain in this cauterization than in others, and I will speak of it later; and it is necessary for the cauterizations on the horns to be more subtle than those done on the middle part of the head, and this is the form.
dou cautere dou chief	The cauterization of the head.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes to a part of the head and spreads to the eye, and the nerve is purged with cleansing medicines, and one has done the other treatments that I have said in the division of diseases, and none of these things are helpful: then one does cauterizations according to two methods, namely from medicine agar and iron.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization of medicine agar is that you take a stick of agar and remove its skin and re-coat it with 1 spoonful per two nerves, and then place the temple where the pain holds in such a way that you can re-place the agar stick under the skin; and when it has been placed, tie and tighten well and leave it thus for .xij. hours; and then untie it and treat it further with the agar paste, and let the wound be like this for 2 or 3 days; then put on a moistened cloth wrapped in a cloth until it is healed.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After that, heal with ointment until it is healed; and if you see fit to do the things of some purging medicines that I have written about or in the treatise on purging medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cauterizing iron so that it becomes hot like this, shape-wise:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a bell or has a small hollow in it, and on top there is a little appearance; and put it on the painful spot, hold your hand and turn the iron slightly, until half of the thickness of the copper is burned; and lift up your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is hidden, and decorates an abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After that, put cotton in a wet thread and put it on the spot for 3 days; then I put moistened cloth wrapped in a cloth, and then heal the spot with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cauterizer called "cultellare", all pointed, and beware of cutting the artery in this migraine which is not ancient.
de emigraine	From migraine.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine as we have said before in the division of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the cauterizations from medicine and iron do not work, then it is necessary to heat the cauterizer called "cultellare" until it is white; and then sign on the painful spot a line half a finger's length long, and withdraw your hand once, and tighten it so that you do not cut the artery and come close to the bone; and beware of the jawbone that moves when eating, and the nerves have regard for it, and spasms may come to the patient, and beware of the bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if there is great fear and especially if one does not know what they are doing, and who is not experienced in this; and leave the work in my way. But I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it hurts in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauterizations do not suffice for the illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize at the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery which has two knives; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of ear pain from coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When in the ear comes pain from coldness, and you have tried all kinds of solutions and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pains do not move, then heat this cauterizer which is called "point", whose form is:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After, point the entire ear that is ill or both ears if the pain is in both, and move back one finger's length from the root of the ear since you have marked the place to lance; and put 10 points around each ear; afterwards cure the place so it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be cured by cauterization is not other than those that move due to phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make a cauterization for appearances that come from heat and spasm of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this appearance of torture that moves due to phlegm, yellow bile, and purgings of the head and gargling, and it does not work, then it is necessary that you cauterize the ailing person with three cauters: one at the root of the ear, and another a little behind the temple, and the third in the juncture of the two lips; and put the cauter on the part that appears healthy, and make the cauter in the area of the head near the ear, above a little below the horn of the head, and one on the temple as long as a finger's length; and leave the cauter so high that half of the cure is burnt. The form of the cauter is:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the form of the cauter is like the small knife that we put before it, but it is a little more subtle and it should be that the blade is a little thicker; after that, cure the place as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it in the way that we have said, and it does not improve, and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauters: two on each horn of the head, one within the head, and one at the place called "vasselz" as we have said before, and cure the last cauter in the mouth of the stomach. And cure it like we have said before.
de litargie	litargy (a type of lead-based medication)
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease it is necessary to give the patient large doses of litharge (yeres grans) and calming pills for the brain. After that, rinse the head of the patient thoroughly, and put on the occipital bone a plaster of mustard which is written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the manner of the cauter: if you make it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is cured in this way, then it is good; and if not, make three cauters within the head descending just to the collarbone, with a span of two large fingers between each cauter. Cure them as the others, and if you see that they need to be joined together, and the patient is suffering, then make one cauter in the middle. And if necessary, make two others on the two horns, and cure them until they are healed; and this is the form of the cauter called "olivare", as I said before.
de la froidor dou chief	The coldness or chilliness of the head.
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of years and what we have said before; after rinse the head of the patient, then make a fire cautery in the head and on each horn, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the illness is strong, make four cauteries on the spine of the back; and let it burn until the deepest part is charred, and lift your hand; after cure so that it becomes sound, and the cautery which is called "olivare" which we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should not use cautery unless the one who is phlegmatic, and it is necessary to cleanse the brain of years and other remedies that we have said in the division when the patient is great and suffering from severe medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot suffer, I make him gargle and chew to cleanse the brain often with good meat; after I rinse his head with milk, and I do one cautery according to what we said before, and one cautery on the skull, and on each horn; and if the illness is strong and suffering, I do cauteries as I said to the one who has paralysis and softening of body, on the spine of the back and neck, and be the olive cautery according to the manner that I said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, I do one small cautery in this way:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When on account of melancholy the superfluities or moistures are corrupted and a gross scab forms, then instruct the patient to undergo a burning with hot irons as we have said to one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if on account of melancholy the superfluities decline to melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink by which the brain may be cleansed, as is said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then again bind the patient's head; then make one cloth of flax well made, also like a circle, if he puts it on his head; and the patient should be crossed and held tightly from all sides; then present the ointment, and mix with old balm beeswax; and heat it temperately so that the oil can bear it; then empty the circle inside on the head, and let it cool down; and do this to the patient once a week each time with another good management, until they are cured.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish to cauterize him, make several points all over the cauterizing iron.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This manner of cauterizing moistens the brain equally; and then put on dampened cotton in butter and goose grease.
de l’awe des eulz	Il semble que la phrase se termine là ! C'est-à-dire "d'eau des euls" qui signifie probablement un remède ou une recette pour les eus (une affection de la peau). La phrase précédente parlait d'un traitement par cautérisation, et cette dernière semble être une autre étape du traitement.
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	Lorsque l'eau (ou la goutte) vient premierement sur les eus par les signes que j'ai décrits dans la division, alors commence à donner au malade une chose qui nettoie le crâne et en enlève toutes les humeurs, et fais-le suer plusieurs fois à jeun.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After the command to hold back his head, and he has a fire cautery on the head, and he has two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of the humor is in both eyes together, or in one eye if it is in one; and cut at all the cautery all the veins and arteries that are beneath the bone, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and beware of bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop with such power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and at the incision the caution how you shall stop it; and never made a cautery or cauterizing beneath the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	from under the eyes (or tear ducts)
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears from the eyes are old and accustomed and are on top of the veins, or near the arteries that are in the appearance of the head outside; and one sees that it is superfluous cold humidities, then he makes the cautery that I said at the beginning of the humour descending to the eyes: one cautery in the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or cauterizing beneath the two bones; and if there is need more, so he cauterizes carefully above the eyebrow with each little cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	from within the eye sockets (or tear ducts)
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you medicate according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit at all, then give the sick person to drink 3 ounces of cochineal wine. Then anoint the head with olive oil and make a cautery with a mixture of the olive oil cautery; and make two clavilis cauteries on both eyebrows, one a little above the eyelashes; and beware not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the parchment of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this cauterizing iron called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	in which shape:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that it has to be done, apply two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrow hairs are; and do not leave your hand there except until one-third of the parchment is burned, according to the manner I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	a single eyelash that points the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	At any time when the eyelashes are converted to stingers and point the eye, and it is done with a cauterization in two manners: that is to say by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	Or the fire cauterization orders the patient to let the eyelashes be as long and even as they are; and if they point at birth, then he must bind them so that they do not move until they have been born.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are even, then the patient puts medicine in his eye; afterwards he places a mark on the parchment of the eye that is as like as a myrtle flower, and it is the beginning of the sign next to the eyelashes; then he puts moist cotton soaked in egg white and perfumed with persillium on the eye; then heat the cauterizer which is the form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards cauterize on the figure that you have marked with a dot and a few more times, so that the charcoal is burned in place; and the sign of health of the eye is that you see the parchment retreating, and the eyelashes raised to the tip of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then put moist cotton in butter as long as the heat is gone; afterwards cure with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the eyelashes come and the parchment is softened then start again with the cauterization on that very same spot, as you did first; and if the lashes are protruding, then cauterize until the parchment is raised to its natural level, and is even, and do not point the lashes at the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cauterization with burning medicine is that you order the patient to let the lashes be as long and even as they are; then make a parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and live coal, each one third, and grind them together well; and do it quickly so that it does not cool down; then spread it on the form you have made like the myrtle leaf, and put it on the eye parchment; and if the illness is in only one eye, then work with one, and if in both eyes also; and put cotton moistened with egg yolk under the eye; and the patient's eyelids should be in their natural state, and place your thumb showing on the medicine, and press once and lift up all the times that the patient feels a sting from the medicine, because it stings as much as fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then take off the medicine with your thumb.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the blister has passed, then remove the top of the scab, and reward yourself if you see the parchment raised just as it would have been raised by constriction of fire or by cutting; and if so, it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, so place again the medicine on the site where the medicine has no effect, until your works are equal, and your eyes put in order; then set on moist cotton wool in a burrow until the hot callosities are gone, after cure the site of anointing which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to take good care of your work by great vigilance so the medicine does not spoil on the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hair pricks in the eye, start again the medicine on that site which is softened by clean paper properly, as you have done before; then cure it until it is healed; and this is the shape of the leaf of myrrh:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And you should know that the eyes of men are diverse in greatness and smallness, and according to these is their constraint; and the right path is not answered to him whose study is this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of a fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to place his head in your lap; then have him place his head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move or change position. Afterward put moist cotton soaked in egg white or persimmon juice over one eye, then heat the cautery which is thus formed: and shape it like the point of a feather quill, together with the handle; if you wish, make it pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, make it also like a tent; but nevertheless, what is shaped in this way will serve for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After press the fistula if it is open, and take out the pus, and dry it; and if it is closed, then operate, and remove the boil. After put hot cauterized instrument on the area around the eye, holding your hand at a safe distance from the cautery to prevent accidents. Then place the heated cautery in the fatty part of the eye and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, have the cautery redone once more, and if you need it again, let it be for 3 days; then put a moist poultice of cotton in a nutshell on it, and apply the unguent of desiccating ointment until they are healed, and if 40 days pass without them being healed, put a corrosive astringent medicine on it until the bone is exposed; and the rest as you would in your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand by a fistula, and cut it out; then put in the opening I, a subtle powder whose form is this:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make it to the size of an egg; and hold your hand or cloth firmly, and do not let the patient move until the blister forms a scab; and it is necessary that someone places cotton moistened in eggs or in oil on the eye of the sick person. The blister soars up to the place of the fistula, and the pain passes through marvelous healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed through the cauterization that we have said, it's good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer pertainum to the patient, and bring the fistula back into the body of the neck according to what is proper in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks on lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Most of the time there are cracks in the lips that are called "pox", and similarly on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks with the remedy we have said in sections, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cauterizing iron according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it hastily in those cracks until it comes up to a point; after that, cure the area with ointment until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	an abscess of the jaw
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the jaw or to the gum, or to the palate, or to the roots of the teeth, and after it has made pus and boils and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in sections, and it does not help: then it is necessary that you have a cauterization according to the size of the fistula. After that, boil or purify the fistula, and hold your hand so that the iron rod comes up to the point of the fistula and to the last part; and do this once or twice, after that cure it as we have said in cures, until it is healed.
dou movement des dens	The movement of the teeth.
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine and it does not help, then put the patient's head in your healthy one; afterwards heat the cautery from which the form will come later in this way that you put a cloth on the tooth; and put hot hastanment inside the cautery and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; afterwards lift your hand and repeat the cautery according to your will; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and let it sit for an hour and a rich foul breath.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was moving is confirmed, and the gums softened are restrained, and the moisture corrupted is dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain of the teeth comes from cold or there is cold or wetness, and medical remedies do not help, then it is necessary to have a cautery in two manners: and a cautery of butter and a cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery of butter is such that you take butter from a cow, and dip the end in an iron or silver spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a thimble, and soak it in melted butter, and put it on the painful tooth quickly and hold until it cools down; and do so often until its virtues reach the root of the tooth. And if you see that the wool and cotton are soaked in cold butter, and put them on the sore tooth, and place a hot iron so that the fire comes to the gum of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The hot iron cautery is such that you take a dog's bone of iron or lead, and it should be thick so that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient; after that, heat the cautery until it takes shape, then place it on the tooth and hold your hand there as long as the cautery is cooling down; do this often, because the pain will go away that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fills their mouth with good butter in anticipation of this hot iron and then drinks a remedy; and this is the shape of the hot iron:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery on any part of the head that you want, and according to what you can do; and this is the form of the ligature:
des scrophules	From swellings.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulas are of cold and moist humors, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then heat the hot iron well so that this shape comes afterwards, and have two openings for the vapors to come out on the other side; and put the hot iron on the abscess once, or twice as often as necessary, until it comes to a head on the abscess; and if the abscess is small then place the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it like that for three days; and apply moist cotton in butter until the inflammation is gone; afterwards treat the wound with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the dogwood:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistures prevail over the channels of the body and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient must be purged first with soluble medicines; after that make a cautery at the root of the throat, and take care not to come too close to the throat, and let it burn just enough.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that make another cautery at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and let the cauter be called "clavicle" as we have shown before; and cure the place just as we have said before until it is healed.

de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder

When the shoulder's joint is dislocated due to moisture and you put it back in place and it cannot stay but comes out again and dislocates by a small movement that happens, as we have proved, then it is necessary that you redress the first dislocation.

dou cautere de pleuresin	of the plague cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that at the plague one should make cauterizations with roots of aristolochia, and in this manner: take a long root of aristolochia as thick and as long as your thumb; and let it be dry, and moisten it with oil, and hold it over the fire, and cauterize 1 cautery between the shoulder blades and the neck, and 2 small cauterizations a little below in the part which is under the beard; and 2 cauterizations between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining backwards by a little; and 1 cautery in the breast, and another on the stomach, and 1 between the two shoulder blades, and 2 on the sides of the breast behind the cautery that is between the two shoulder blades; and do not press your hand, but make it open as when smelling.

de la mice	of the mumps
