Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure, when it has been neglected for a long time, and this is considered worse than the other cures previously mentioned.
de ydropisie	Une autre spécialité !
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	The cautery does not help in dropsy, except by means of what is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure it according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your cure does not help, then it is necessary that you make 4 cauterizations around the mouth, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen, and 2 behind the back on the spine, and one next to the navel; and let the cauterizations be well near the spine of the back.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cauterizations to ooze and get a good burn for a long time, and do not neglect the sick person's treatment after the cauterization; and healing will hasten, and both intentions (i.e., the physical and spiritual aspects of health) will be restored together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be a key (clavicle), as we have shown before. And that for the back should be an olive-shaped one, according to what is written above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of inflammation of the eyes (blepharitis)
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsical, and are full of yellowish pus, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the ring finger and the middle finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And don't go too deep inside; so as to avoid a severe burn, thus shape the cautery according to this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Afterwards, make two cauterizations on each leg at the point of the cuticle (i.e. the nail bed); and let the cauteries be long, one in front of the knee joint and the other behind it, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries to ooze for a long time without curing them, until the pus comes out; afterwards cure with the other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	of menstruation (menstrual irregularities)
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the womb comes from cold and moisture, to the point that the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestine are dulled, and cannot be cured with methods of treatments; and you see the sick person very suffering and of great virtue, then make one large cautery on the stomach according to what is said above about the stomach cautery, the circular cautery; and 3 small cauterizations around the navel subtlety to each one of the key-shaped cauterizations subtlety, and 2 cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistors abundant and the sick person suffering, then make a cautery on the navel, and one cautery on each side of it, and 2 small cauterizations on the stomach next to the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids (emorroides)
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the ulcers are at the fundament, one or more, and are old and are thick, cold, and moist corrupted humors, and they are treated as we have said in divisions, and it doesn't help, if you do a cautery: III on the spine of the back, that which is all over under the nape of the neck and in triangulating, and I cautery under the mouth II to be desired; and if you think the stomach is cooled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees swelling in the face, then on the face I a great cautery on the stomach, as it was said before, and I another on the liver, and I another on the belly with the whole cautery sharp; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment let the place heal as long as it is sound.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the disease of "thelul" (a condition characterized by growths or tumors on the skin)
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you strike with the steel, if it heats up the cautery which seems like a razor, and then puts it all on fire above the steel strike; and I leave your hand as long as the cautery comes to the birth of the vein, so that the blood flows out; do this once or twice, and if there is much flesh, cauterize each part as we have said; afterwards apply ointments which are beneficial until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a great cautery on an abscess, it will have greater help.
de plaie mal curee	a badly cured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot suffer cutting or opening, which we will tell about in its place, then this disease comes that cannot be cured except by cauterizing.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula comes and is swollen and emits foulness and corrupted moisture, then you should probe into it as carefully as possible, and make sure that you know to what depth it goes.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heat the cauterizing iron until it is red-hot, and insert it into the fistula according to the depth that the probe has entered, and reheat the iron as long as the foul and corrupted flesh are burned, once, or twice, or three times, depending on the severity of the case; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are nearby, and the large blood vessels.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the bladder and the intestine, be careful of those places, and do not apply such treatment unless on a place that is charred, and think it is not a purpuration; after treating the place as long as it is sound, and if the site is sealed and the materials have been removed for a long time, then know that the site is completely healed; and if the materials are not removed, know that the site is ulcerated and corrupted with rotten flesh at the bottom; and thus as one of these we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When a cold pain comes to the kidneys and there is severe flatulence, and it does not take on the characteristics of a woman's menstrual flow, then you should cauterize over the kidneys with one cautery and on either side of the cautery needle that we have spoken about before; and if we are going to cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a row, and they will provide greater aid.
de la vessie	the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and soft from cold and moisture, and the patient retains urine, then you should cauterize in the area above the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, and one to the right and one to the left, each cautery being as long as a thumb; and do one cautery behind, or two if needed; and make the cauteries needle-shaped according to the form described before.
de la marris	the uterus (in this context, likely referring to uterine issues such as prolapse or other conditions)
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the uterus is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception, and the flowers (likely referring to menstrual flow) are corrupted and their ends are delayed; and when they come, there is great pain: then it is necessary to make three cauteries around the vulva, just as we said about cauterizing the bladder, and two cauteries behind; and make the cauteries needle-shaped, just as we said.
de la hainche	the anus (or possibly "haunch", referring to the buttocks or lower back)
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moisture descends to the back of the anus, and because of this the patient has difficulty sitting in their usual place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the area of departure from the normal position is found, then it is necessary to cauterize the sick person above the back of the anus with one cautery resembling a circle, and make a mark before the site around the back as it turns, so that the back is inside the circle; and the cautery should be like those used to treat the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not present, then make three large olive-shaped cauteries (likely a reference to a type of cauterizing iron), and the cauteries should be as deep as all the kernels; and cure it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	the pain in the anus
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the joint of the hip, and it is due to coldness and moisture, and the patient is treated according to what we said in the division, and the treatment does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purify the patient with thick, fetid pills or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is thus in two ways: that is to say with burning medicaments, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is in many ways, one of which is: that you cauterize on the hip bone three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make good depth and size, and have between each cautery the thickness of an egg, and be the cauteries olive-shaped; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on the head of the hip, for which reason there are four according to this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that the cauterization has reached the cautery of the circle which we said before in the dislocation of the hip; but do so in such a manner that the circle contains all the hip and all the flesh of the knee is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And it is the manner in which one does this in sciatica, when the pain remains in the hip and does not reach as far as the thigh or as far as the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes as far as the thigh and leg, then you make two cauteries there where the patient says that the pain is located, and one cautery on the ankle four finger-widths away, to the left a little; and be the cauteries cutlet-shaped, and be the thickness of a key ashed; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as two inches or nearly to the knee, then cauterize there where he feels the pain three points or four at the cautery which is called "point".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, you make more of them; and if he knows that the pain is under the kneecap towards the thigh, then you cauterize at the cutell-shaped or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauterizations that you do not tear the cautery so much that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause more great harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have had a fire cauterization on the ankle of the foot, and they let it grow so that the leg was completely inflamed, and the feet as well, and it was perforated and corrupted with all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purging of the belly from which he got death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a cauterization on one and on the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men said concerning the cauterization of the groin, from what this is the manner: Make such an iron rod and it should be as thick at the top as a date stone or a little less, and it should be between joints and from one joint to another it should leave the quantity of an almond kernel; and the joints should be two parts over, and they should also be like almonds, and there should be a groin iron well made; and this is its shape.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be warmed until it is entirely red and smells like onions, and then place it on the cleft of the patient's groin and turned towards the good side; and cauterize once with a hot cautery and let him rest for three days; and then make an ointment with butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the cure of anointing until he is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim said that we should use the pot of this cauterizer for fear of his glance, and see a pot who uses it; and yet these are good cauters, which can bear it, and where it afflicts.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The burning cautery of medicine is this: you make an instrument between the bars in which it descends to the edge of the door, and it be of brass or iron with one layer long, and in its height have two nubs, and between each one have the quantity of the thickness of a finger; and they be open on top and bottom, and join together according to this shape.
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Then place the burning brazier on the patient lying on their stomach with one side of their hip towards you, and press your hand hard on the brazier; then throw between the two circles of hot iron that has been heated over the fire a small pot, and let it be there for an hour of double time, and suffer the patient to feel the heat and burn of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it finds also mummification with fire; and when the application of heat has passed, you lift your hand with the instrument and raise the hot brazier off the patient, and let it be so for three days, and place on a poultice as long as the scab from the burn is stripped away; and leave it there for three days until the ulceration disappears; and that would be the last aid after the treatment of ointments as long as they are healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	If the pain has spread to the thigh or down to the leg, make the instrument that holds heat as you have done in the hip exactly; and this is the method of hot application, and I wrote it in the book of rectification of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take lime and live coal, as much from one as the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	If there is a small hole in the back so that the point of a razor can enter it; and put on top of that pot another pot well weighted down, and put hot coal and lime and sweet heat on top, until there will be two powders above them which you will have well prepared in your hand; and leave it thus until the warm liquid and the scum come out into the leaden pot, then take all this liquid, and pour it onto the coal and lime so as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very swollen and is administered in various works of medicine and cauteries of other members. For it makes a hot work like fire, and if there are other medicines with which one cauterizes well the groin thus as thesis and honey from almonds and calx with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment by which a man was cured of the pain in his groin and sciatic vein, and he greatly praised it, and says that no other treatment was done to him, and that he was healed at once when this treatment was done, and he had bathed himself just as he teaches us here afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in this manner that you take a fresh and dry green verdigris, and grind it very well with one part of fat, and put it on the groin and thigh and leg where the pain is, and bind it; and let him be for three hours and by as much as the patient feels no more burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then let him enter into a bath until his body is somewhat warmed up, and have him enter into bed, and the pain will go away altogether and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	Know that no one should use a cautery on such medicine unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with fire of goat hair, it greatly helps him; and it should be done in such a manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and beat it with old oil, and place it on the hollow between the thumb of the foot and the other one that is called foscule.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After take goat hair that is dry, and hold it to the fire until it is charcoal, and place it on the linen, and let him lie so until he is stained; and do it again thusly, and never cease doing thusly until you think by sense that it will come just up to the groin, and that the pain will be ceased; and this manner of cautery is called "cautery of goat hair".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, or by falling or concussion or from too great evacuation, or from appearance of cold matter spread, none of these appearances is worth cauterizing, unless it comes from infusing cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that after these the patient be freed from fetid pills or other similar things, and one make them on the back, there where the pain holds, three lines marked with ink, and in each line five cauterizers or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can bear; and let the cauterizers be made according to the cautery which is called "points"; and if you see, do three cauterizers or four at the middle cautery of nails in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a tight umbilical cord when it closes, and fear; and you will find in the last spine of the back and on the appearance that comes above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it heal, then cauterize at the cautery of that place in this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery of purple fire is applied to each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, then cauterize around the spine with the burning cautery two lines or three, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Afterwards, cure the place so that it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not bring the cautery near a tenderness which is in the way of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints are due to moistors that spread to every member of the body, and when the pain comes in feet, which the physicians call "podagre" properly, and when it is of cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, so it is cured by cauters in this manner: make a row of cauters around the joint of the foot, and be the cauters olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you prick on the face of the foot, then let the face cauterize completely with all the cautery which we call "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the knee and to other joints, and this happens many times, then let the cautery be done on each knee three cauterizations or four of each part, to all the cautery olive-like; and if you need more, then do more, but do not hold your hand away until the splinters of the cure are burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend as far as the knee and to the back, administer the cauterization that we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the tumor 2 lines; and if there remains no pain, make points over each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come as far as the armpits or as far as the shoulders, cauterize each part, and do good management to the patient and give medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you do him good management and bleed him, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the spleen.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the rupture comes in the groin, and the belly descends to the testicles and it's new, so it's necessary that when you see them healed, don't irritate him that day; and let him do things which relax the stomach, so that the pain descends from his stomach; then make him sit on his back between your hands, and tell him to take a deep breath until the belly is settled, and wipe with your hands, and sign over the incision under the rupture above the bone of the elbow, and do all at once, which will resemble half of a circle above the body; then heat the cautery in which there is the form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and it discharges pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reassemble the intestines to their place; and have someone else hold his hand so that they do not go back in; and work well on the thighs of the patient, and put a cushion under him and a servant above the thighs, and another above the belly who holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign at the whole hand, and keep it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again once more as long as you continue until you reach the bone; and beware carefully that the intestines will come out when you are doing the cautery, so that you do not burn them; and that through this the patient does not die, or another evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that whenever you do not come just to the bone with the cautery, your endeavors are worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery for children be subtle according to their size, and for grown people also as large as their measure; afterwards cure with butter ointment at the place of the cautery for three days until the scarring is removed; afterwards cure with other salves until they are healed, and let the patient lie on their back for forty days so that the wound be well sewn; and it is necessary that the stitches be left for a long time, so that the swellings do not protrude when he will prepare to go into chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And afterwards when he wants to get up, have him brought a well-made bandage and wear it for forty more days; and take good rest, so that he doesn't overwork himself and beware too great repletion of drinking and eating, and too high fever; and when he does this instruction then is completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say hereafter the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Of the twisting of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers come in other wounds and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then make the fire cautery at the cautery's root according to its quantity, and let the third part of the cure be burnt; after the cure as we have said; and none of the ancients said that one must cauterize it with a cautery at III angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first make the sign of the end and make a line across its width over the ulcer, and another below it, and with your hand inside hold the whole cautery steady.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and more gentle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, either from falling or cutting, and that pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine is not worth it, then it is necessary that he be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and let the cautery be according to the length of the member and its narrowness and weakness and virtue and location of its twists and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed from the first cauterization, it is well; but if not, repeat another cauterization on him, for this custom is that he must move to the member that is closest to him, so you should make the cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of wound-making (or surgery)
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The moles are helped sometimes by cauterization with great aid, and just as the disease comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see it being cauterized, be careful if the disease is at its beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not spread or remain, and you doubt that the corruption may infect the whole patient, then do 5 cauterizations on the head: I in the middle of the head, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the eyebrows; and II on both horns, and I behind on the occiput; and leave your hand there until the cauterization reaches to the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors may issue forth; and cauterize on the nape according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the wound is scattered all over and it's clearly failing, then you should cauterize with the same set of cauteries that we have described for the head, and one more on your navel, and two on the spine of the neck, and six on the spine of the back, and one large one on the croup and another on the belly, and two on each shoulder, and two on each thigh, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands. Be careful not to burn the nerves that are on the hindmost part of the calcaneus, so as not to cause any damage.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that when I do more cauterizing, I make the treatment more helpful; and know that the patient does not feel pain from cauterizing as healthy people do, because their body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterizing be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in ways of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the treatment place flour on it several times with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes in any member and is treated by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then make cauterizing on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cauterizing be one part going into the depth of the furrow; then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And any time made is cautery to the hand and foot and back at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus if it is an abscess; and nevertheless no one meddles with it unless he is knowledgeable about the members and exits of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	Of the remedies
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease that is called "albaras" is inflamed, and the art of medicine does not help anything, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the quantity of the best sulfur, until the scab is removed and its color changed; then cure it with flour of chickpeas and lentils with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of cockle and blood of almond, each one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and keep it in place until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure for syphilis by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a cancer comes at the beginning, and you see it arrest, if you cauterize it with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the border of the cancer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And in any case the wise said that you make cautery also in the middle of the cancer; and yet it does not seem to me good, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen once; and it is more correct that it is cauterized around, with the cautery that is called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	from the swelling that cannot be killed (i.e. syphilis)
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has an illness called "adubelati", and it delays their death or due to the superfluity that it causes or because of the age of the patient when they are decrepit (that is, too old) and they have a lot of blood, or because of the cold; and you see them hastening to die: then cauterize him all around with many small cauteries that prick; after let him be thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to dying.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see that the cauterization is piercing through at every point, then heat the cautery until it has this shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the midst of that illness called "adubelati" until the cauter is pierced the skin, and be such cauters that the patient feels them outside in such a manner that the course of the ulceration is opened up.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After, heal him until he is completely sound.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure by fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of illness is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a gangrene of the member, for it corrupts the members just as fire corrupts dry threads.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can bear cautery together with fire, then heat up the cauters small and large nails somewhat; afterwards cauterize from all sides as much as you need to scrape out all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupted be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for 3 days, and put on the places that have been cauterized some poultice with oil as much as the scalds from fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the ointment cure generates a boil.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after 3 days that a healthy boil does not arise, it is good; and if not, then re-cauterize on those places that remain corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this mixture is sometimes been cured of medicinal poultice in place of fire cautery; but nonetheless fire cautery is a greater help, and I have already said the cure of the medicinal poultice in its section: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	une infestation de poux à pieds
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Much of a time it happens that on the feet by forensics a disease arises which is called "closed" according to our intention, and it is a large abscessed thing that wounds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization of this disease is according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cauterization, and cauterization with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cauterization is that you heat the cautery like a pen of vinegar, and it should be made of good iron to the measure that it can pierce the abscess from all sides, and have subtle edges; after that put it very hot on the abscess, and turn your hand entirely around the abscess until it reaches the point of the abscess; and leave it thus for three days so long as it starts to discharge pus; then make an ointment of bitter wild savin bruised with oil, and leave the ointment on all night, and the abscess will burst and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the place with ointment by applying oil until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if it is converted by being outside the body, and occurs many times in hands and feet, then you should bring in hot water cautery; and similarly: take an iron or steel shell, or a feather of copper, and put on the nail and the wart, that is to say porridge warts; and place the shell on so that it seizes everything around, then put a little hot water in it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand by turning so that the edge of the shell comes to the root of the nail, and the hot water penetrates deep enough to the root; and let the patient suffer a little the burning of hot water for an hour; then leave it, and it will be completely detached from all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So do this after another, until you have extracted all those that are within the body, then treat them with the ointments that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the cure of trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from cold or nerves, or quartan fever or other, it is necessary that you do for them 4 cauterizations or 5 on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one on the foot, and one on the stomach at the olive-shaped cauterization point; he will leave off trembling, and hasten to health from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	the boils or buboes.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes appear on the outside of the body boils, or foul-smelling pustules, which come from large corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	Then it is necessary at the first sign of them appearing to make a fire cauterization on the head of each pustule: a subtle fire cauterizer made from a staff of myrtle wood into which the point has been grasped by the fire, or from a long root of Aristolochus, or a lentiform cauterizer.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes when you cauterize them at the beginning when they appear in this way, and they cannot grow any larger forward, but rather the superfluities from which they come are broken down and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great hemorrhages of blood from the artery that is cut in the wound that appears first, or at the incision of the apostema, or at the cauterization of the member, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet whenever this happens to someone, if you hurry and put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and strain it hard until the blood is calmed under your finger, and no more blood comes out; then set on fire several small and large olive-shaped cauterizers as many as they are red; then grasp one, either great or small according to the wound and the place in which the artery runs, and put the cauterizer on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cauterizer so long until the blood is stemmed.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if the blood spurts out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauterizer is extinguished, then take hastily another one of the cauterizers that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the blood is stemmed; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other evil comes upon the patient; and know that when blood pours from an artery, it cannot be well stemmed on its own when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways we have said: or by cauterization, or by extraction when it is not closed off, or by tightly tying a thread, or by applying medicines which have the power to stem blood; and let it be tied and strained in good time.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will remind them of stemming the bleeding by tightly tying a thread or putting hot things on it, or similar things, if they do not know how to do so themselves?
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and he does not have a surgeon or medicine present, then he should put his index finger on the wound of the vein as we said, and strain it well until the bleeding is stemmed above the wound and above the vein; and he should not move his finger, but dampen it with cold water often enough that it becomes very cold, so much so that the blood congeals and thickens and is stemmed; and make inquiries in advance for what he needs in terms of cauterizers and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical remedies.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all illnesses for which a cautery of fire or hot medicine is needed, along with the reasons and causes and tools and forms of cauterization; and I placed that chapter as an introduction just up to this point, and I will go through this chapter in the same way so that what you want to find is more easily found.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I may begin this, it is necessary, my dear son, for you to learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first one about cauterization, and because of this it is necessary to be even more careful.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there is often evacuation of blood when opening the wound, and at the incision above the abscess, and with the treatment of wounds, and at the extraction of splinters, and at the incision on the bone, and similar things; or doubt and fear, and death comes to many.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you must not undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from those who have so afflicted themselves with their illness that they would die easily because of the foolishness they find in their sickness, and because of the greatness of their wickedness; and of these one should be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are some who give you their counsel, and say: "Wait, I am healed"; and the sickness is deceitful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more trust in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not give foolishly but wisely to those of whom you are certain, and from whom you can have taken and received something; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients whose salvation is converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dearest son, Our Lord grant you good understanding and integrity, and if you will it, inspire you with the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen. (This is a typical way to end a medieval text, often used by monks and writers as a prayer-like closing.)
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter in sections, as it is laid out before the chapter on cauterization, which I have divided for you from beginning to end, so that you may find more easily what you will need. (This is a conclusion to a medieval text, where the author explains how they have organized the content.)
dou chief plein d’aigue	Full of water. (This phrase seems to be a heading or title, possibly indicating that the next section deals with a treatment involving immersion in water.)
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease often comes to children at birth, and when the midwife holds the child's head too tightly; and sometimes it comes from a cause that is unknown. (This text appears to be discussing a condition that can occur in newborns.)
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this disease occur except in children, and in all that I have seen it has hurried death; and because of this, it seems to me that it is worth less the effort to treat them in such cases. (This text suggests that the author believes the prognosis for infants with this condition is so poor that treatment is not worthwhile.)
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose temples were filled with water, and the head was swelling every day so much that it couldn't be supported; and I thought it had died already, and this death is caused by an accumulation of liquid under the bone above the sphenoid sinus, between the skull and the bone; and if the work is such that the liquid is between the skull and the bone, and the abscess is small, then you make a cut in the head which is wide enough to follow the shape of the abscess:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the liquid is more swollen and the abscess is larger, then you make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the signs that are the corners of the head open on each part, and the sharp point springs forth when you press it with your hand from inside, and this does not respond: then you must cut into the head three cuts in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision extract all moisture outside.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After secure the openings of linen and powder, and put wine and oil on them, and leave in this way until the fifth day; then loosen it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and let the head be tied equally, and give food to the patient dry meat from a place of moisture as long as the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look to see where the size of the aposteme opens up, and the meeting place of the sharp point; for it is sometimes in front; sometimes at the back; sometimes on the right side; and sometimes on the left side.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So then cut there where the aposteme opens up and the filling of the sharp point, and the flesh according to what you can manage; and be careful not to cut into the artery; and come out with blood flow, so that the patient dies from the bleeding of blood and the evacuation of moisture.

Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone a disease which is called "catarre" in the eyes or on the private parts, and the patient has been sick for a long time, and medical treatment does not help, then the final cure is cauterization with those things that will close the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then, when you cover the eyes, the patient should turn their head back; after rub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then extract the patient's neck from the whole cloth; then see where the vein bites, and the places of one and the other are afterwards the ears, and they have been replaced; then mark the places with ink; then cut one and the other with a sharp knife so that it comes down to the bone, and this is by the length of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, put the thread needle under the artery and tie it above, cutting also like two threads across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is tied, then it will jump out continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the vein does not open to the touch, it is necessary that you measure the length of the space of three fingers, then signify [to] fill and make just up to the bone; and what needs to be put out of blood is VI c., and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the refilling of the vein; then look at the wound: if it remains over the bone point with syphac, see that suppurating apostemes do not come in, then close the wound and tie, and apply ointment for cure until it is healed.

When it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that you fill the place with old cotton and lay on well-made tents; and when you untie them, be careful to apply dry medicines that cause flesh to grow and tents until they are clean; and if blood spills from the artery as long as you work, hurry to cauterize by fire, or you fill the place with vitriol and hold it in your hand so that the blood is stopped; and if you do not have these things present, lay on the place your cloth as much as the blood is congealed, and wash the place with cold water until the blood ceases, and be careful as necessary.

dou reume des eulz	It seems like you're quoting from an ancient medical text.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste. de la char des papieres	of the flesh of parchment

de la gresle	of frost
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come to the eyes of the patient things that seem like frost in their form and hardness, and because of this is this disease called "grandine", and it is an assembly of thick moisture on top of and below the paper; the procedure is such: take care if the grandine moves from one part to another, and it is a light thing to know; do therefore on either side, then scrape off each part lightly, then take it up with tweezers, and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing the paper first, then harm nothing to the patient; and if the crack is large, assemble with a seam, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not use force, for the ointment will restore it at once and knit flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine is descending inside the ear towards the top part, then turn over the paper and have the grandine held with a pair of tweezers, and cut it off and press from one side to the other; and if the paper is pulled away by the incision, that does not harm anything. And when the grandine has been cut off, then clean out the ear with salt water, and cure the place where the growth was, until the patient is sound again.
de la graisse des eulz	of earwax
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. des poilz des papieres	the hairs of parchment
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on parchment that are not natural and are infested, and they harm the skin, and cause various diseases such as constant tears and softening of the parchment and spots, so much so that it is a cause for the destruction of the skin; and the cure according to four ways: or by cautery together with fire, or by medicine hot in accordance with what is said before or the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by cauterization, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the patient's head in your hand, then turn the parchment of the eye towards your left hand; if it has been converted, that is good; if not, I will insert an awl into all one thread above; and have this near the margin of the parchment where the hair grows next to these hairs, and lead one thread above all the parchment, and turn it at the razor; then make a small incision in the part below the parchment, below the infested hairs, right up to the big tearer down to the little one; then draw out one thread, and put under the parchment a small patch of cotton and cloth; then sign above the parchment a figure of tinder, such as the leaf of myrtle, and whatever the figure is necessary in proportion to how much you see the parchment that has been separated from everything.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if someone has need of it, one should apply a great quantity of paper that is softened;
