and if not, then have no care for it, then leave the suture and the threads until three days or four; then treat the wound without sutures with drying and constricting things, for the paper revives at the solidification of the wound and the assembly of it, but the suture is muddled (as said the ancients), and this work has no fear; and there is another way: that you mark the paper with a figure such as the leaves of myrtle, as we have recounted, with three cut wicks according to the shape which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then place the ones that rise to the small joints evenly according to the shape that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	If you do not have the power to hold the forceps, and the thing is not perfectly even, take a needle with one thread on it, and insert the point into the figure; and pass the other thread alongside the large scar, and the second thread alongside the small one, and tie between your hands the threads evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin over which you have marked, as we have said, then bring together the two edges of the wound by suturing, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe with cerote and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hairs on the paper are converted: so you must use what we have said about incising; but the suture in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of wounds is according to this form: and it is that you fold the paper and make a hole in the center according to what I have said, and then make two stitches by art, and two fine threads as long as the width of the paper and its breadth; and place the two ends of the threads on either side where you hold the strings; then assemble one and the other subtly above what rises from the paper oil, and strain the two stitches from the two parts together; and let it be like this for some days, and the skin that has been strained will die and turn black and wither away until it falls off.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, if the wound has good forces, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound is sutured, and the paper has been lifted up, and the hairs will no longer be prominent; and this is the shape of the two dogs that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	You take a fine needle and insert one silk thread that is very thin and fine; then tie the threads together gently, and let the length of the threads be about the breadth of a hand; then place on the head of the patient one more fine silk thread briefly, and bind the ends to the head of the thread; then have the patient put his head under the sun so that the operation is clarified, for this is a subtle and minute operation; then insert the needle into the entire length of the skin at the root of the hair adjacent, and make it pierce quickly through until you draw it out from the natural hair above; then pull out the thread with the hairs until they are all in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the thread is drawn and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will draw the thread from below into all the silk threads that you have placed there, until the thread comes out through the hole above and you see it with the sight of the eye; then you will draw out the thread and the silk thread, close up the eye and let the eyelash alone for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh appears; and if the hairs are small, accompany them with one long hair from the natural eyebrows, and raise it with that which you leave, as long as it is elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet ! La "porriture" ou la déformation de l'œil est une question médicale qui était étudiée à l'époque.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness which is called "aleacrati" or the scabbing comes to the eye, if there are two types of it: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And occurs by a sudden blow of a wound, or an incision, or a cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of treating it is that you cut open that wound, and separate the lips of it, and put inside linen tents, and tie so that it heals; and it is not necessary to use in its treatment things that dry up and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the illness returns worse than the first; but it works with softening things, such as fenugreek; and rose of water or althea root cooked, and ointments made from distilled aquilol in some oil, and I envelop a tent, and treat with those.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care so that it does not heal back in the form it was before; and these works that we have said are not other than warnings for this illness, that it will return in the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	A fragment from a medieval text about eye problems! The phrase "de la char qui vient en l'oil" roughly translates to "of the flesh (or membrane) that comes into the eye". This suggests that the text is discussing conditions related to ocular surface or conjunctival issues. If you'd like, I can try to provide a more detailed analysis of the text's content and context!
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is under the [joint] which truly is called "axacrati", and it is a natural and an accident.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from a wound and a cut and a cautery and similar things; and the way of doing this work in it is that you take a needle, with which it has two threads, and the point goes into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left armpit to the right, so that the threads come out at two holes in the flesh; then stretch the skin above over the whole needle, and the handle as far as the spatula is wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the appearance of the paper comes back as it is supposed to, that's good; if not, take a razor and put it in the cut, and turn the paper, and make two cuts or on either side inside the paper; and be the holes of the two cuts at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and be made one angle so that when they are assembled, the appearance will be like that of a letter which is called "I griesche"; then remove that skin, according to the amount that its edges are cut off under, from what is left on the paper; then join together the two severed parts, and sew with one thread of linen; then follow the cure of those things which we have said about mollifying medicines and tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from an incision or a cut or a cauterization, it is fitting that you make a flat incision below the fibers of the paper, and according to what has been said before; then separate between the two layers of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the operation according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise master craftsmen prepare an instrument of all their power to make the figure return to its natural form; and the sick person himself, according to what it seems fitting to operate and with instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet !
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this inflammation occurs in many people in a similar manner as the paper above is stained with the white of egg, and cannot move or do its natural functions, then you must insert the point of a razor underneath the paper, and lift it up; and keep steady with tweezers until you cut what is stuck to the spatula so fine that it is not too sharp nor too coarse, so that the patient can suffer when the spatula is too sharp or burns the eye; and your incision, which you scrape off this assembly, should be light, so that the paper returns according to its natural shape; and the whole assembly will heal, and sometimes in the eye there may be salty water and the discharge of white mucus, and then put a linen cloth between the paper and the eye, and put woolen cloth moistened with egg yolk on top of the eye; and after three days cease using the collyrium and all similar things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	The conjunctiva of the eye.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	It appears that the conjunctiva of the eye is in two forms: it is nerve-like and resembles a hard scab, and another which is not nerve-like but resembles white congealed moisture. When you touch it with iron tweezers and try to pierce it, you cannot; and both appearances begin near the large tear duct and grow slowly, bit by bit, until it covers the whole eye, sight, light, and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	It seems that the method of incision is as follows: the patient places their head in your lap, then opens their eyes. You lift up the paper with one hand, and with tweezers of small double-pointed forceps, you pierce the conjunctiva above the lid line. Then, take a needle, and insert one hair from a horse, cow or ox, along with a strong thread. Double the point of the needle a little and insert it into the conjunctiva, then push the entire needle through and tie the conjunctiva with a thread and lift it up. Scrape off all the hairs on the side of the conjunctiva that touches the eyelash and the mucous membrane down to the head, then cut the remaining part in the root of the tear duct with a fine spatula and small forces. Leave the natural tissue of the tear duct so that through the incision, the usual course of tears is not interrupted. And sometimes tie the conjunctiva only with thread and needle, as we said before; then scrape off all the roughness of the same form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And take care that the spatula does not touch the sensitive tissue and break it, and that the eyelash is not pierced. And after the incision, pour into the eye a little of burnt silk thread and litargiric ointment, and let it stay until the next day; then cure it with what is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not numb, and you cannot prick it with a needle, and the awl cannot enter it, this resemblance of a nail is often cured by medicines; and there emerge just as I have told in the division, and if you see it cover, take care to cover the eye of the patient, and take a light spatula with a sharp point according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And reset the nail above gently, and if you see it does not decrease and the pain presses there, then distill from your mouth into the eye a cord made of mercury and red salve and silk thread, and stop the eye just until another day; then resume the other work according to the same deed, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If any thing is against you in the eye, as an abscess forms, then milk it, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work just as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid hurts in the eye with great harm, then suspend it to the awl, and clip a part and not all, so that no tear comes out; then distill into the eye red salve which is made of mercury.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	...pour les oevres dou larmier, et les ungles qui croissent en l'oeil.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Red blood appears in the eyes of some men sometimes, and covers the eyelid and holds steady above the pupils and turns towards the outside, and seems like a rose from red stone; and the work is that the patient puts his head in cold water, then opens the eyes, and takes out all the red blood with needles suitable for this, and sustains it with force; then cuts the first layer of skin, and goes on cutting to the razor's edge until the end, and be careful not to harm the eye during the operation; and let the incision be so small as we have said in the incision of the eyelid and with the gentle forces that one uses when extracting a thorn, as the form after this chapter shows; and when the incision is completed and all the red blood has been removed, then put oil of sarsaparilla or similar corrosive medicines on the eye from which the blood was extracted, and put cotton on the eye outside with egg yolk, so that it becomes secure against a hot abscess; and if there remains nothing, and the bleeding is stopped, and you doubt a hot abscess, then leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with soothing things for a hot abscess; then return to your operation until it is healed, and thus do when red blood is lodged in the eye by this likeness.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	Mais il faut toujours aller plus vite dans le traitement d'un œil faible par la voie naturelle, et par la voie accidentelle à l'aide de fer; et ne jamais mettre ta main dans aucun de ces ouvrages tant que tu ne vois pas que ce membre souffre en raison de cet ouvrage.
des voines des eulz	of veins of eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	They are red swellings that cover the eye, and prevent vision from working properly and weaken the eye forever.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary for the doctor to first look at whether the eye is free from the swelling, and if there is no other outer disease of the eye apart from the swelling; then tie it in such a way: instruct the patient to put their head in your hands, then hang those threads all around the circumference according to your wisdom, and let the threads be thin and double according to this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And be two threads of a degree apart from each other in one circle in this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then carefully twist those threads together and squeeze out the blood every hour after another, until you see the foreign veins being removed from the eye; and be careful not to prick the eye with the points of the forceps, and do this task at midday in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you don't harm anything except those veins; and when you have done this, let green and red juice drip into the eye to corrupt what remains of the vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to finish the task in that hour, make a poultice on the eye with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it on for several days until the pains have subsided and you are sure of a feverish outbreak, then resume the procedure as described above until it is healed; and this is the shape of the forceps:
de la fistule de l’oil	It seems that the text has ended with the phrase "de la fistule de l'oil", which translates to "of the eye's fistula".
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The physician so calls "arissati" fistula: when you cure it by cautery and hot medicine as I have previously said, and it is not healed, then there is a plan in place that you incise above the abscess, at the spot where it must die, and drain all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, then replace it with all the instruments that make up this form; and it is called "aspre chief", and should be made of iron like a sharp chisel, and should be pointed as with a file, just as it appears in the present shape:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the spot of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your hands, and press your hand a bit until you know that the corruption is reduced; and do this as often as necessary, then restore the place with caustic medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the abscess is closed and pus has formed, and the body of the boil is closed and remains in that state for 40 days, and it does not reopen and is not an abscess, and there are no other bad occurrences, then know that it is healed; if not, since there is no other cause than to bring the fistula back to the navel according to this form: and is that you uncover from the bone the second time by iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it has been uncovered, take a stick according to this shape, and let the head of iron have three angles, and let the handle be thinned down to the top as you see here:

It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait as long as you can to extract it, for it should not be done hastily; for it is a very high substance, and one must have no excuse for pulling it.

Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain will depart from the patient and they think it is due to the catheter of the good saint, and make them urinate with the catheter; and nonetheless the pain does not leave by this means until the bad thing is extracted, for we have already seen this in these saints; and when you are certain about the catheter, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth on all sides with a very sharp spatula to guard the gum from everywhere; then move it with your hands or fine forceps in the first point and point until they are well extracted, then secure the forceps well; and the patient's cheek should be between your teeth and keep it steady so that it does not move.

After you extract the tooth properly without breaking it, and if it will not come out, then take one of these instruments and push it inside from each side lightly, and move it just like you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and bruised, you should fill it with cloths, where the hole is; and if it's strained gently with pincers so that it doesn't break when straining; and you must carefully operate around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful that you don't break it, and leave a part of it, and tell the patient through the wickedness of the root he will have greater pain than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful that you don't act in the same way as foolish physicians who through their haste and recklessness break the tooth sometimes and do not bring to it what we have spoken of; but instead they often cause great illnesses from the roots that remain or from the tooth that they break, as we have seen so often; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the place with vinegar or with oil and salt; and if bleeding comes from the wound which often happens, fill the place with powdered vitriol; and if it doesn't help, cauterize it.

de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root of hair remains behind at the edge, it is necessary that you put on the place moistened cotton with butter one day or two.

quant li dent lochent	Quant li dent lochent (When the teeth decay)
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth is loose, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press up against what they chew without it falling out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines but this does not help; so it is necessary to constrain it with a thread of gold, because the silver threads become green and rot, but gold never changes; and the middle thread should be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you want to bring together the teeth, take the thread and insert it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the loose tooth between the new teeth, if there is one or more, until you will have brought them into place safely up to the healthy tooth from the other side; then re-cover the covering up to the part where you began, and restrain your hand subtly and carefully, so that it does not move; and keep your finger at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then tie the threads of the thread together with pincers, and assemble them, and reattach between the healthy tooth, and put it so that it does not wound the tongue; and then let it be tight as long as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the threads break, have it tied by another thread; if it remains and serves thus for its whole time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens. de coper lou liien de la lengue	De couper le lien de la langue (To cut the ligament of the tongue)
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes it is this string that comes under the tongue or naturally, when one is born thus; or by accident of a sewn-up wound; and the work is such that you operate on the mouth of the patient, and have their head in your own sound tooth, and lift up the tongue; then tie the nervous cord of the length so that the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, it is because of a sudden wound, so put an adhesive plaster and tie the cord of length; and be careful that the fissure is not too deep, for the artery which is under; and when you have done this, then lift up the gum with a rosewater and asafoetida, or cold water, then place under the tongue a linen tent; and let the patient fester every night, so that the wound cannot soder.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding comes from the wound, then apply verdigris on the place of the wound; and if the blood flows out, then cauterize with a slow cautery lentigo, which is good for such things; then cure it with another cure until it be healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the wound is of a foul colour or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards blennorhea, and there is moisture, extract the pus and make a thin poultice from it and deliver the wound from one part and another; and if the blood comes to your work, put on vinegar plaster as much as it needs to be stopped, then return to your work until you bleed all out; then lift the swelling with oil and linen, and treat it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	swellings of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come down the throat small pouches called "godath", and they are properly called the "almonds", and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard abscess of little sense and green color, do not touch with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. And they should be sharp on one side and blunt on the other. Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born inside the throat, namely the small sense abscess; and I had well closed all the throat, so that the woman could not exhale because the passage was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have been dead if she remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had risen so high that it had burst through two pores of the skin.

Then I hastened at once and inserted an onycha in one of the pores, then the flow came out, and a great portion of pus came out; then I refilled the other part into the other pore of the skin, and opened his mouth and pressed his tongue; after that I inserted the onycha into the abscess, and cut out a piece, and only a little blood came out; and thus was unblocked the passage of the throat of the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease cutting from this abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing again, and filled the place that I had emptied, so much so that it became very large; then I bound it up and cauterized it inside the throat: thus he remained without growing; and I left those places, and knew only what God did with him after me.
de l’uve	of the urine
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». li chapistres des apostemes	It seems we've moved on to a new topic.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay perforation until it is dead, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the fundament, then if one pierces it when it is dead; but it does not behoove that you pierce an abscess which has become crusty without its digestion being completed, except for that which is near the fundament, lest it rot deep and become a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.

And it is necessary that you know the sign of perforation of an abscess that is dead according to completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the reduction of fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the cessation of movement and inflammation of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you perform the perforation in a place more dependent on the abscess, and where it emerges with pus; and the length of the incision should be as long as possible, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places where there are no folds.

des scrophules	From swellings.

Those scrophules that hold uselessness, pierce it where it most hurts; and pierce in the same way as the one previously mentioned, from above, then pour in tenting with ointment and similar things, so that what remains of the corruption corrupts them; and when the wound is well cleansed, apply ointment to the ulcer until they are healed.
de squinance	A single word to translate:
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones spoke and said about the cutting of the throat; but I never saw in our land anyone who did it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have suffocated, it is necessary that the incision of the throat which is called "epiglote" be cut out; and this is not done by others, because all the veins and the pulse of the patient are warm near the abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pulse, it is necessary to cut out the epiglote to avoid the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary then, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it under three circles or four a small incision through from side to side, between the two circles or by the quantity of the incision from side to side, not in the cartilage; and those places are suitable for cutting into the epiglottis since there is no flesh, and the vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretch the skin of the throat to the entire neck, then cut the skin as far as it will come, and extract the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then close the cut with a dressing, just as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the cutting of the vein of the neck which bursts through the place that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a time.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which we doubt strangulation, gather together the two lips of the wound of the skin, and sew all together except for the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	We must not do this surgery until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be on the verge of death, and the pulse is faint.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then close the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this reason the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malignancy of the disease had passed, and it had passed in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took the knife, and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the channels from the womb; and I was summoned to heal her, and found her dead as such.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found blood issuing from it, and I knew that she had not cut too close to the vein nor cut deeply enough into the throat, and the veins were issuing forth through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried, and sewed the wound, and healed her so that she was well again; and it happened to the young woman that she did not speak for a long time, and returned to her usual condition afterwards; therefore I say that in cutting into the epiglottis there is no cause for fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the throat (or more literally, "of the big throat")
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called an "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in color like jet stone, and it occurs mostly in women; and it comes in two manners: natural and accidental; or natural does not have a cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident occurs in two manners, of which one is similar to fatty nodes, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it must not be operated on with fire unless it is small, and you prove and search for all the surrounding tissue: if you find it just like I do not see fat, and it cannot be opened in any way, then cut it, as one cuts fatty nodes, and dress it with all its covering, if there is none; and search well thoroughly, and heal it just as it should be, until it is perfectly sound.
des nous	of tumors (or swellings)
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways belong to us, from which I will say all similarities; and now it behooves me to say the entire difference that is between our dislocation and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an abscess is hot and feverish, holding heat until the boiling point has passed, and then it reaches its full purulence; at which point the fever and heat subside. (Note: This suggests that an abscess is characterized by a hot, swollen, and possibly pus-filled condition, which eventually resolves once the infection has been fully cleared)
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the nout there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it swells in its sac, which is its own sac and is according to the colour of the body, and begins like a boil, and becomes large; and they are either hard or soft, and much coloured as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is fitting, when you come to treat the tumor, that you should first examine and investigate it thoroughly with all the instruments which are called "intrumentarium" (or tools), according to what its form will reveal, whether it be a head or chapter that comes after. (Note: This suggests that before treating a tumor, one should carefully examine and investigate it using various medical tools and techniques, in order to determine the best course of treatment)
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring into abscesses of joints is that you take or the most moist part that you find in the abscess, and turn your two probes back and forth until you know that the instruments have pierced the core, then as much as it is according to the size of the abscess; then draw out the instrument, and be careful lest it bursts over.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture condenses on the core, regardless of its color, do it as I have said for other abscesses; and if afterwards the poultice does not bring forth moisture, know that it is fatty, so then do it in a cross shape, and take hold of it with pincers, and scrape off lightly from each part towards the coat where it lies, so you lead it out healthy with the needle; and if you cannot lead it out healthy, then lead it out in pieces so nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing remains, it will come back repeatedly; and if there remains a small piece and the blood grieves you, then apply some sharp corrosive powders to the wound, and bind the wound tightly, and put on soothing things such as hot poultices, and cure with other treatments until it is healed; and if the tumor is large, cut off the two edges of the wound, and cure what remains of the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein that bathes it is in opposition to you or another thing that hinders and you hurry to apply vitriol poultice, and let it be there for two or three days, until the wound purifies, and the effusion of blood subsides; then return to cauterizing what remains of the tumor. (Note: This suggests that if the vein is in the way or another obstacle is present, a treatment involving vitriol poultice may be necessary, which involves applying a poultice containing vinegar or vitriol to the area for several days to help purify the wound and stop bleeding)
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Behold the forms of the inserted instruments, and they are in three manners: great and middle and small; and among them there are three square ones that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and among them there are three manners: great, middle, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistula; and they are also like the needles with which one sews suture, and they are made of yellow tin, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are most tried for piercing black blisters to enclose the cores of fistula; and they are in three manners: great, middle, and small, according to the quantity of the largeness of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the needles are in various likenesses, as you see here: great, middle, and small; and there are needles that have two cores in three manners also; and there are needles that have three cores, and they are also in three manners; and there are needles with one core only, and they are in three manners; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these cauteries is cutting, and among them there are those who do not cut more than one part, from which the nerves are scraped; because one does not open the vein or the nerve; and among the introducers are the linen strips that respond to wounds, so that the patient is not hurt when opening abscesses; and they come in three sizes: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one must not use more than what fits, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling the scraping of splinters, in this shape, to staunch blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and we place it sometimes in the location where there is bleeding from incisions of veins and arteries, and sometimes we make it in this large shape. (Note: This suggests that the tool may be used to stop bleeding from specific areas or locations, such as near major blood vessels)
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of certain men become swollen when they begin to be corrupted, so that they resemble women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and those who want to cure them must apply according to this form from line 2 to line 8.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat and fill the wound with medicine in the form of charcoal. Then bring together the two lips of the wound at a seam, and care for it until it is healed; and if the mammary gland hangs low and is swollen like that of women, then make two compartments above it by two similar incisions, so that one contains the other at the end of both, such that the larger line holds the smaller according to this shape, up to the line .b. just to the line .g.; then scrape off the skin that is between the two lips and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about seam and powder and everything that is necessary in the care, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not yet fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or for the discharge of blood, then you must fill the wound with moist cotton in corrosive ointment; and leave it so that it softens the remaining fat and flesh, then care for it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses on the armpits. (Note: This appears to be the title or heading for a section of text that deals with treating abscesses in the armpit area)
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that occur under the armpits are types of hard scrofulas with tubercles, and there are some that contain moisture. (Note: This suggests that the medical professional is describing a type of abscess or skin infection that occurs in the armpit area, and may be related to tuberculosis or other inflammatory conditions)
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be bound according to this form, from line b to line g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been emptied, then fill the wound with fresh cotton and let it be like that until the next day, then remove all the cotton and treat it with ointment suitable for such things until it is healed. (Note: This suggests that after draining the pus from the abscess, the medical professional will apply a layer of clean cotton to protect the wound, and then allow it to rest before removing the cotton and applying an ointment to promote healing)
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to a scrofula, then do it in incisions like we have said for scrofulas, and if the wound starts to bleed again, then apply cauterization as we have said before. (Note: This suggests that the medical professional may also use a technique involving incisions or cuts, similar to those used for treating scrofula, when dealing with abscesses that resemble this condition)
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of an artery. (Note: This appears to be the title or heading for a section of text that deals with treating a specific medical condition related to blood vessels and arteries)
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut and the skin is sewn up on top, there are often abscesses that form, and just as well there is blood flow and an abscess; and if one knows how it happened when it's from the artery, then the abscess is long inside and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, then you feel it clearly; and when it's due to the vein, then it's a reason to be outside apparent; and it's foolishness to cover this abscess, and especially when it is under the armpits and in the groin and around the neck and in many other places, and it's very great.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to cut the cautery and that one who is at the head must also cut it, and in that one who is due to an inflamed artery, make a cut above the skin as long; then work the cut along the incision, and carefully separate the artery from the veins, until it is uncovered; then put under the one needle, and make it pierce up to the other side, and restrain the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then mark the place that is between the two threads with a small pointed instrument until the blood issues which is there, and release the abscess; then apply the dressing that has been mixed with balm, as long as the thread is hanging; then treat those with ointment suitable for them, until they are healed; and if the abscess is due to the incision of the vein, it is necessary that you mark on your hand what you can take from the abscess over all the skin, then put the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and there will be a double thread, so that you pull it out from the other side; then tie the abscess with two threads of the thread as I have told you, or the thread of one of the two parts to the two eyes of the thread; and if you doubt that the strings will not issue forth, then put another needle under all the thread of the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and restrain the strings in four places; then tie the abscess until the superfluous issues out, then tie the superfluity of the skin and leave what is tied; then apply a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, then treat them with compresses and ointments as long as they are healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses in the neck. (Note: This appears to be the title or heading for a section of text that deals with treating abscesses located in the neck area)
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just like abscesses that come in the artery and vein, abscesses also come in the neck when they are ruptured, or due to excessive work, and similar things. (Note: This suggests that abscesses can occur in the neck area as a result of trauma, overwork, or other factors, much like they can occur in the arterial or venous system)
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	It occurs most often in the shoulders and arms and in all places where there are joints; it is also a painful swelling, and its color seems like the color of the body, and it appears in many dispositions without pain; and when one presses on it firmly, the patient feels pain, but it is not deep within the body, but under the skin; and it can move well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor downward or upward, and that which occurs in joints should not be cut with iron: perhaps there would be a contraction; and he who has it on the head or on the forehead, makes a pouch out of leather.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is small, one holds it with pincers and cuts it at its root; and if it is large, one suspends it by a thread, and scrapes it, then removes it and stitches up the wound to the suture, and cares for it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Hanging large lips.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the stomach and not elsewhere throughout the body, and it is a disease called "fungus" by its resemblance to them, and there are thin roots and large heads; and there are small and very great ones; and I saw one man who had two of them in his stomach which were more similar to fungi than any other thing, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a small root, and were split open, and it flowed with moist liquid at once.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found that one weighed 18 ounces, and the other weighed 6 pounds; and the operations for incision are such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the abscess is white and moist and has a thin root; if it bleeds heavily, and you are present with the cautery by fire.
