de la circoncision	Circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a disconnection of continuity like the other wounds; however, when we make this work of our own free will and properly for children, it is necessary that we do the best work and the easiest for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	Je dis que les anciens ne dirent pas que la circoncision devait être faite pour leurs enfants, car ils n'en ont pas mentionné dans leur loi, et nous n'avons d'autre chose que ce que nous avons acquis par expérience. (Traduction : Je dis que les anciens n'ont pas exigé la circoncision pour leurs enfants, car ils n'y font pas référence dans leur loi, et tout ce que nous savons sur le sujet est issu de notre propre expérience.)
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Car j'ai vu la plupart des maîtres et des sages qui faisaient la circoncision autour d'un dal (un pot de cuivre) ou avec un couteau de force, et tout une nouvelle aiguille ; les coursiers fuyaient car il y avait deux pointes, et par hasard si l'on coupait le dessus et demeurait celle du dessous.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Maintenant la recovient (la circoncision) est coupée, et le douleur est double, et avec la saignée du dal il ne est pas assuré que le pointe du membre soit coupé ; et avec la saignée de l'angle par hasard l'on escappe le fer, et l'oeuvre (la cicatrice) court, et maintes fois naissent des cicatrices qui n'ont pas besoin d'être ménagées.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Je n'ai pas trouvé que la saignée faite à force avec un couteau de force ait la bonté de l'expérience, car les forces coupent juste autant bien en haut qu'en bas. (C'est-à-dire que le résultat est indifférent et sans intérêt)
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Car when you press your hand, if it bleeds evenly in all directions; but that the string be well stretched around the skin; and the manner of the first operation is such that you make the child think, if they understand, that you do not give them more than to tie the thread around the penis only as much, and then let it dry in all ways that you can; then hold the penis straight between your hands and repeat the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the children do not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand on the penis and blow or squeeze, and pull it up as high as the head of the penis comes out; then clean well of the filth which is assembled there; then tie the new sign with a double thread, then tie under one ligature to another ligature; and hold with two thumbs through the second ligature on the pouch and at the first finger's indicator, and push between the two ligatures; then lift the keur up quickly and pull out the head of the penis; then let the blood clot and dry, for that is the mores; and put powder on it and on top of the powder glue a cloth with a beaten egg white, tempered with rose water, mixed with good fresh rosset oil, and leave it on until another day, and cure with another cure until they are healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The forms of purgation are thus: the two hands should be clenched and stretched, and the hands should be as large as the wrists equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of purgation is when the roots inside come out through the incision; then you should stretch it to your finger nail so that the place makes an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingers, take it in tongs, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they persist for .iij. days, and that which is under the penis becomes swollen, then leave it so long as the abscess will heal, and scrape it lightly; then cut it as you can move, and keep away from the part of the penis, and it will do him no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound with sudden powder, which we have spoken of in treating powders, and if you cut from the root too much, and it goes up, it will do no harm; then cure it as we have said, so long as it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	The retention of urine.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to congealed blood, or frozen blood, or bladder stone, or kidney stone, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see it is retained because of a stone stuck in the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be bent over on his knees; and his feet should be placed on his back, and he should extend his belly from the top to the back, and restrain the patient's loin as long as possible; and then constrain the neck of the bladder to express itself through the stone above, so that the urine is released. And if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should administer extraction using all the instrument called "syringe", which is in this form: and it should be a thin and lightweight silver thread, like a bird's feather; and it should be half a palm long, and should be fine at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the extraction of the urine is such that you take the double thread, and tie it to the head of the flax or cotton wick, and put the end of the thread into the syringe; and trim off the excess of the wick and push it up to the head of the syringe. Then anoint the syringe with oil, tallow, and egg white, and have the patient sit on a stool, and moisten the bladder and penis with damp oil and olive oil and aloe juice; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, as far as it reaches to the root of the penis. Then fold back the skin over the body, and insert the syringe forward up to the bladder, and let the patient feel it coming close to the empty thing, and this is not done in that order for nothing, but because the conduit through which it goes is twisted; then hold the thread tightly with both hands, and the urine follows the thread, then pull it out and make the urine flow. And start again with the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and have the patient lie down.
des maladies de la vessie	diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When bleeding or pus comes into the bladder, or putrefaction has set in, and you see the urine become cloudy and medicated, then do this with all the equipment that is called "clepsydra", and it looks like:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the place is covered by which the medicine should be such that it stops the urine very well without addition, so that we can draw out the moisture, and push when needed; and when you see putting your medicines in the bladder, put the head of the catheter in the moisture, and pull on the drawing who is inside; if you will pull out the moisture into the catheter, and then push back strongly the drawing inside; if the moisture goes inside, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of subtle catheter by which we catheterize the bladder: thus it is.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or horn, and the head is higher up; and below to one breast where the cord falls; then take a sheep bladder and put in the moisture you see catheterizing the bladder, then tie between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat that pouch over the fire; then put the head of the catheter into the penis, then strain your hand on the bladder to all the moisture happening, so that the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make one circle, and pierce it roundly around; then put the thread strongly in these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a lock, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie up the instrument; and do so as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	from the stone (or perhaps "about a stone" or "regarding a bone", but likely referring to a kidney stone, given the context of medical treatment)
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already described in the division the ways of stone and the extraction together with medicines; and said the difference between the kidney stone caused by rain and all the signs, and in which stone we should operate with surgery; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone that is formed in the bladder happens more often in children, and it's a sign that the water has jumped from the bladder resembling the subtlety of urine; and I will open it, and the surgeon grates the patient's penis, and the patient urinates many times, and then it swells; and there are many such jumps in its foundations; and is light the healing of children until they have .iiij. years, and it's very grievous in old people, and it's more common in young men, than those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones, than those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with a cathartic, in order to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For sometimes it obstructs the ability to extract the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and throw him down and move to underneath, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes come out from very high; then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downwards; then seek and touch inside; if you feel the stone in place, then hasten now to cut above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall to the touch from anywhere, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is feeble, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young adult; and push it into his fundament, and seek the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, bring it up to the neck of the bladder; then press upon it with your finger, and push it out further ahead there where you see cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the surgeon to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to extend his right hand to lift up the scrotum, and with his left hand remove the skin that is under the scrotum in the part where you are making the cut; then insert the surgical knife, which is the shape... (il semble qu'il y ait une lacune dans le texte)
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	Between what is between the testicles and the fundament, not in the middle but on the left side of the nave; and it should be straight up to the bone, and the handle of the trephine should be at the fundament, and the head of the trephine should be such that it is wide behind and narrow inside, according to the size of the bone, not too large; by chance the pressure from the handle which is on the fundament might cause it to jump out without effort. And know that there are some bones where there are angles and edges: these are hard to extract; and those which are smooth, resembling a pear, and rounded, whose extraction is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	To that bone where there are angles and edges, make the head of the trephine larger; and if it does not jump out, then you should extract above with pincers which are also like a file at the top, to loosen the bone so that it does not escape; or you place beneath the instrument curved at the top; and if you cannot engage it thus, you should enlarge the hole little by little, and if the blood is spilled, then you constrict it with vitriol; and if there are two bones, then push in first the largest one into the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then draw out further, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if they are very large, then you must cut them off, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either they die, or urine comes out often because the wound cannot heal itself. But nonetheless try to extract it, or to cauterize with tongs, as long as you can pull it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, then bind the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and tie it tight, and put on top of it a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to calm the hot abscess; then raise the patient up onto their neck, and do not untie the band until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, the wound should rise up very well with oil and water; then treat it with defenicion ointment and basilicon ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses and ulcers come in the wound and corrosion, and congealing of blood in the bladder, and so retain urine, which is collected in such a way that it does not pass with the urine: then heat your hand in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder, and harm it; then raise the wound from water and ashes and gauze, and help the patient in all ways you can, until they are healed; and it is necessary that all the works that you cure them with, that you bind their two thighs together, and assemble the medicine on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the channel of the penis, and stuck inside, and the urine cannot come out; so cure this with what I say thus: that you let him make water many times, and excuse him from making a cut for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proved it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod, shaped according to this form, with three spikes fixed into one stick.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and tie it around the penis above the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then insert the rod into the penis lightly, as far as to the stone; and turn the rod in your hand from the top to the bottom, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; and soon the urine will come out, then press your hand up on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken at once and leaps out with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie the thread below the stone and the other above, then make a hole in the penis between the two threads, then pull it out and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood which is in the wound; and cure him until he is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the woman's stone (i.e., kidney stones)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It often happens that stones are found in women, and if it ever does happen, the cure is grievous, and is prevented for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is because there is no well-skilled woman who would be willing to expose herself to the physicians, especially when she is pregnant.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman lies deeper than the stone of the man, why it must make more deep incision, and great fear is there. And if necessity summons you to do this, then you must take a midwife well knowing, and with much pains find one, and if you cannot find one, then cast not mire subtle; and present yourself before a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her that she does what you command regarding the incision of the stone; and look very well if the woman is a virgin: then you must push your staff or fundament and seek the stone; and if she finds it, then constrain it under her staff, and recommend that she puts her staff or on the patient, and presses her left hand upon the bladder very firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then it must be moved gradually from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then tap above the bone in the root of the thigh against the middle of the cox, where the swelling appears, and feel the bone in that part; and do not move his knee above the bone or below, and make a small incision first; then insert the probe into the incision, if you feel the bone so close to the wound that the bone can come out freely, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and rounded, and with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the appearances in order to know how it will come out.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the stone escapes, put vitriol powder on it and hold it in place for an hour until the stone is suppressed; then return to your work, until the bone is free, and have instruments that I told you about in the extraction of stones from men to aid you in your work; and if the stone escapes, and this is due to the artery being cut, put powder on the place and strain of tents and bandages, and do not touch it again, and leave the stone and do not pull at it, lest the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the site is quieted, then return to your work, so that the stone may be heated.
de hernie carnouse	A swelling of flesh
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non. de l’aposteme des coions	of an abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme. Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from the body, and indeed from the testicles; and it is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine. Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches. de l’aposteme des coions	of an abscess of the testicles

Then sew the two edges together with a stitch, and if you see fit, sew first the excess of the soft skin at three stitches or four firmly; then cut between the stitches, and cure it as other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of the treatment or management of a condition related to punishment, possibly referring to a medical condition caused by physical punishment or abuse.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You should know that castration is forbidden in our law, and for this reason it would please me not to speak of it in this book; and it is only necessary for two manners: one is that the physician may know how to respond when asked about a cure, and how to perform the cure; and the other, because we often have need of castrating certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castration is done in two ways: either by pulling, or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by pulling, we make the beast sit in warm water until the testicles are softened and during this time; then taking them with your hand, until they return to normal and you can no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The chastisement of the tail: it is necessary that you stain the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and strike above each orifice at the scrotum, when you have thoroughly scraped them; and let there be no scar tissue either thick or thin which remains on the vasa. And this manner of chastisement is more certain than that which is done by attrition, because at attraction something may remain from the testicles, by which the beast desires lust; then heal the wound until it is sound.
des hermofrodites	hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermafpodie is according to two manners in men: one is when between the two testicles it also opens as the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes in the court it urinates.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has on the paps as a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of an ulcer and a woman's womb is that you cover the joined-up stitches all over, and treat them as other wounds; in the second manner, men whose urine shoots out through the skin of their groin, have no treatment.
de la tentigene	from epilepsy
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The tentigo is a joined-up ulcer on the natural part, as long as it is so ugly to see; and some women also have it as large as a hand, and that is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you dye the superfluity of the tentigo to your hand or fingernails, and cover it lightly; and do not go too deep lest there be an outflowing of blood, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed; and a certain ulcer that appears at the mouth of the uterus, and apply a poultice, and by chance bursts forth, and is similar in appearance to a cow, and because of this they used to call it in ancient times "cow sickness".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	You must copy it, as we have said the tenacula, and the treatment until it is healed.
de erratique	Je crois que c'est une référence à la maladie d'Érasistrate (ou Erratique), qui était une affection sexuelle connue dans l'Antiquité.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is erroneous if the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the womb is small; and it is innate by birth, or an accident from disease that has come upon it; or it is caused by a stuck thread, or a subtle or thick clot, and it is formed deeply in the uterus, or on the sides, or below, or wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and perhaps makes her have periods; and knowledge of this comes from looking at the belly.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is a near appearance, it appears in the breasts or on the chest.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle clot and it appears close to the navel, hurry and do this: place your two thumbs together, and have the woman be on her back with her legs spread; then grasp the navel firmly, so that the subtle clot comes out, and the swelling goes away; then take linen, moisten it in oil, and put it on the spot, and let the woman rest at home each day, so that she cannot close.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the scalp is hard and thick, it must be shaved to the skin resembling a mulberry leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of flesh only, suspend it with a cord and shave it; and have antihemorrhagic medicines such as alum, dragon's blood, incense, and egg whites together in abundance; then apply a large linen bandage so that the wound cannot heal itself; and thus be left for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen; then cure him with other remedies until he is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when there is flesh formation in the marrow, it must be shaved according to this manner, if it's not a hardened abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an infected abscess in the marrow, one should not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	Voici la traduction de la partie consacrée aux emorroides :
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Varicose veins are openings of veins whose blood normally flows freely, and when varicose veins become old they become thrombosed; and we have said in the division their similarities, and signs, and I will say here those which receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the thrombus, when they are deep inside the rectum, and do not appear to the touch, there is no cure by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the entrance of the rectum, which one can feel, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary to put the woman in a cold room, then burn the thrombus with pincers, and cut off its roots, then powder over medicines that restrain blood, such as aloes and dragon's blood and frankincense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the buttocks for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if there is a hemorrhage of blood, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate rinds and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and asafoetida, and make an ointment on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he holds still, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him endure cupping at the back and shoulders without hitting him; then take linen, and soak it in juice of plantain or in juice of hawthorn with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has settled, then treat the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a sharp headache, so cover it as I have said to do for the head; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the throat.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come into the marshy places, such as carbuncles and hot abscesses and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other illnesses that I have said in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary therefore that I say in this treatise the hot abscess which comes to the marriage, which is not among the abscesses that burst forth; and if you want to know how to work with iron, look to see whether the abscess is inflamed at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not rush to pierce it, but let the abscess become numb as long as the pain is eased; and then make the patient sit on a bed, and have two small stools so that he leans on them, and lean on his back and assemble his legs towards the part of the outside leg; and be his thighs spread out, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good cord; then place the handle towards the right side, and bring to him the instrument with which one works at the mouth of the marriage, from which this form comes afterwards; and it is necessary that when you see bringing in this instrument, that you insert the first peg in order to know the depth of the abscess, so that what enters into the instrument does not come further than it should, and does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the abscess with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and it is necessary that he puts the cone of the instrument above, and that he moistens the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess bursts open and is handled with soft hands, it should be covered with a cloth at the head, with a clean linen cloth moistened in rose oil or green oil. And put the cloth over the wound deep within the marrow, and put a clean linen cloth wetted in water or cooked mallows on the outside of the marrow and on the elbow; then cure after two days of ointment as needed until they are healed; and sometimes lift off the marrow and the wound with a cleansing of water and honey, and then water or roots of lily and long aristologe cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is reopened in the marrow, you must beware of cooking with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Je m'excuse pour la réflexion précédente. Vous semblez avoir voulu me poser une question sur le thème de l'enfantement.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the woman to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are such that when you see the woman approach labor below, and desire to smell the armpit: then hasten the fetus to issue forth in force; then understand that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the issue is under her chief, and the placenta with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly on her belly, so that the fetus issues quickly; for when it ascends above its head, the placenta comes out with it, and the mother's superfluities are expelled by good purging; and what comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes comes out on her feet, and issues forth from the body or the head, or hands, or comes up on her belly, or behind, and is converted by chance over her neck, and through other evil forms; then it is necessary for the woman to be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures about how one must help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out with its head first by natural delivery, and the woman gives birth easily, and the strength of the navel string is weak, then make her sit on a stool, or women hold her; and warm her nature with oil or fenugreek cooked, and then put the midwife between her shoulders a little spatula, which is in the shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And rend the second birth passage, and cut to her fingernail so that the moisture which is inside comes out; and press the woman's stomach until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must have the woman take a poultice of fenugreek with sesame oil; then have her press and strain in the conditio, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: now the child will issue.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands issue forth, then you must have them reset gently bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a stool, and lift her feet up high; then lower the stool to the ground, and take hold of the woman so that she does not move; and if the hands still cannot enter, and the child is dead, then cut the hands with the knife which was put before, and extract the child, and reset equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the birth of a child onto its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes onto its feet, it must be pushed upwards; and then turn it little by little until it is even; then take hold of its feet and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps as high as its hips, then command it to hold, and let it strain with effort; if it jumps higher, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it doesn't jump away as we've said, then turn it slowly back and forth, until it is in accordance with the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be loose.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, then take muscilage from althea, and oil of sassafras, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; and put on the natural sign of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then let her sit in a hot bath up to the armpits; and when she is moistened underneath, then make her wear a girdle of myrrh, and put it under, and let her stay an hour; then have her sit on a stool, then have her strain and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press the belly, for now the child jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child on her legs.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the infant comes into this form, so put him in a basin of water very little and little; then bind him up to his neck, and let his feet hang down below, and be bent over by the bed; and fold his hands little by little, and then grasp them on the belly, and take away the pillows beneath, until she is prepared below; and if the infant does not jump, take his feet and bend them strongly, then bend the belly upwards, then put your hands in; and swaddle the infant little by little; and command the woman to take herself so that the infant comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the birth of the child, whose hand is coming out wide
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to try to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, make the woman get up and go; if she cannot go, make her lie on the bed and have her legs straightened then administer the musilage that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on the stool, then try to bring back the hand; and swaddle the infant according to the natural figure, and make her spit it out, and command her to take herself so that the infant comes out further.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the exit of the child on its neck, and have spread out its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the patient take hold of his hand, then turn it slowly and gently; and when it is even, so place the natural ointment on the elbow as we have said, then instruct him to move it slowly; and when you have done this, so seat him in a chair, and command him to grasp it; and then he must stretch.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for all the second birth (i.e. if there are twins).
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it happens in this way the second time, so cut the navel string at your nail tip, until the moisture is emptied; and if the child can reach its face and neck, so cut off the navel string from the mouth, so that it is not retained, and kill the child; then put the child inside, as much as it is necessary, and command the woman to grasp once: then strain lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the birth of twins. (This seems to be the end of the text)
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Be aware that twins are born many times, and occasionally three or four are born; and this is not an unusual thing, it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	This is a strange thing, and does not live at all, if it grows in abundance; I know those, that they are multiple, and are torn apart by the suction which divides them, which is joined to the mouth; and sometimes come out just naturally as one would say, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue grievously, then the cure as we have said, and the vein is subtle, and do quickly and lightly what it does; and do so as it is worth for saving.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the first month I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than fifteen, and are all formed like an infant by the measuring of wise and glorious ones, and it is necessary that the vein knows all this, for possibly such a thing has happened; so do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you cure the woman of the dead or unborn child, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to operate with hands; it is necessary that you know if the woman has natural virtue, and whether there is an accident or she fears death; it is necessary that the woman be seated on her back, and have her knees inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the midwife applyes a compress of two parts, or it is tied to the bed so that it does not descend with the birth of the child; then rub the mouth of the uterus with moist oils with a mixture of aloes and fenugreek and flaxseed; then anoint the hands of the vein with these oils and mixtures; then put them into the uterus lightly, then wait for the first part to come out or she puts in the compress that is convenient for this, and take note if the child comes down on its head; if it does descend, insert the compress into its eyes or in its throat or in its mouth or in its palate or under the beard or in the navel or near the sides, and if the descent is on the feet, then insert or prick them at the same time with both hands; and it is necessary that you apply the compress to her right hand, and put the crown between her left hand's thumbs, and put it into her entire hand lightly, and insert the compress in one of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the shape of the compress:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then place the needle in front of the other one, or a third if you need it; so that the extraction may be even; and then straighten it evenly while moving from one side to the other, so that the needles may remain fixed, as is its form.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, apply some of its oils to the handle with one of your fingers, and insert it into that part, and pull the other part; and if nothing remains, place this needle or another higher up and do so until it comes out entirely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and it cannot be brought back for the straining, you must wrap a cloth over it so that it comes out completely; then tie it at the joint of the foot or on the knee, and do likewise with the other hand, and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and he is narrow in the neck, or he has a sharp chin assembled, it is necessary that you push the spatula spiny between your fingers, and make the head flat and extract the sharpness; or you will scrape with the instrument which is called "almidach", from which the shape comes with instruments or this chapter which follows this one; and similarly do if the child has a large natural head; and then draw out the bones with pincers, and if the joint pops out and it holds to the forceps, so it will be split, until the pus that is in the flesh issue out from the skin; and if it cannot come out, cut it with pieces at the mouth that you can see; and if it is inflamed on the belly or under the ribs, it is necessary that you bore perforations until the pus flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the baby is above its knees, then the attraction to the navel string is light and the cord's approach to the mouth of the uterus is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if he is narrow in the belly or breast, it is necessary that you draw him out to the wrapped cloth over his hand; and make the belly or breast, until the pus that is there flows out; and if another limb are cut off, and the head remains, push a needle into her palm as far as possible and draw it out until the mouth of the wound; then put in the thread or cord, and draw it out; and if the mouth of the wound is reduced for hot abscess which has come, you must not trouble with, but rather apply moist and greasy things; and apply ointments, and use soft and soothing waters.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the infant is on its side and you can place it even, then apply what we have said to a living child; and if you cannot do that, then bind it with pieces of cloth, and leave nothing uncovered.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the swelling comes that we have said occurs in abscesses that come in the groin; and if there is discharge of pus, then it should be placed in a tight water bath, and apply other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly contained a dead child, then she conceived another on top of that one and rejected the death from the other. (This implies a case of superfetation, where a second fetus develops while the first is still in the womb)
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came to her mouth and swelled so much that it burst open, and began to suppurate. (This suggests a severe case of gumboil or carbuncle)
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was summoned to the patient, and I thought for a long time, and couldn't find a way to heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on strong attracting ointment, and out came a bone, and after some days another one. (This implies that the abscess or wound contained multiple foreign bodies, such as bones)
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was amazed greatly, because a stomach [i.e., belly] should not have bones in it.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought that the bones were from a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I stitched the wound, and applied splints to it for so long that the woman was in a better condition; and the woman lived for a long time in this way, and finally had a piece of bone in its place from the start; and I have no record of this chapter being done except because, when the master finds an unusual thing, he knows how to take care of it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	From returning the womb to its proper state.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the preservator, to whom we owe the books; and in two turning pages, at the two feet of the two lions. (This suggests that the text is now concluding with a description of its physical form, including illustrations or decorative elements)
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Despite that, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the stem is 2 fingers wide, and the margin of the trees must be, and long half a palm and a half; and in between the two hinges there are two adjustments of the same wood, which are firm in both, half a palm long or a bit more; and these two adjustments are placed inside the mouth of the metal for opening when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, with its resemblance more subtle and lighter, is made of boxwood or ebony wood, according to the shape of pincers; and has two hinges, as you see, a palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you see open the metal in all the instrument, so have the woman sit on her bed, with feet stretched out and legs open, then put the two hinges together in the metal, and hold the head of the instrument under between her thighs; then work your hand over the entire instrument, as you did with the pincers equally, according to the quantity that you see open the mouth of the metal, until the woman has what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all topped and have multiple shapes; and when the masters have prepared them, then the work is done more hastily and is more high to men for their quantity. (This implies that the instrument-making process has become more sophisticated and widespread)
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	It does not discourage the instrument that you have not prepared it, because their need is not excusable. (This implies that the surgical instrument is essential and cannot be neglected)
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second child is retained at childbirth, you must instruct the patient to retain her breath, and then let her hiccough with conditio, and hold her hands to her mouth and nose; and if she jumps for that reason, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, you take a cloth and make a hole or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the uterus, such as calamint, rue, anise, camomile, cassaliaigne and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then tie one end of the cloth to the pot, and the other head into the mouth of the uterus, and let it hang until the vapors come down into the uterus; then make her hiccup, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the placenta comes out hastily. (This suggests that the remedy has been successful in facilitating the delivery of the placenta)
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this treatment and does not miscarry, instruct the woman to wet her left hand in sesame oil or in muskellunge oil of althea, and then insert it into the uterus, and wait for the second child; and when she has found it, take hold of it and stretch it little by little straight ahead, so that the uterus does not contract during extraction; but you must move it lightly to the right and left, and then pull; and it will come out and be delivered.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the uterus is constricted, we have said the treatment for hiccups, and fumigation of herbs; and if it does not follow all that we have said, then be careful not to harm further; but it behooves what is at the mouth of the uterus to bind it to the navel of the woman, then cleanse with a tetrafarmacological ointment; if it will calm her and settle, and come forward; but however, when she has calmed down there comes bad smell to the stomach and head, and hurts the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore it is necessary to make convenient fumigations for this: none of the old ones have tried fumigation with dried basil and figs. (This suggests that the treatment being described may not be a traditional or well-established one)
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which we fumigate the woman at the retention of flowers and placenta is this: (This implies that the description of the treatment is about to become more specific)
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is to be observed that it looks like a burn, and one places the head of the caustic in its nature, and the limbs wide on the fire; and there are fumigations above the coals, and the scab until it is consumed, and then another begins.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament (This implies a specific technique or procedure being described, possibly related to the treatment of the woman's reproductive organs)
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Most children are born who do not have the fundament pierced, but rather it is blocked by a subtle membrane: so then at birth the cord should pierce that membrane with its tip, and not let it pierce from sharp metal point, and fasten the wrapping so it does not touch; then put on linen soaked in wine and oil, then apply ointment until they are healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.
