And if you doubt that it will stop up again, then put on a linen plug or cover, and let it stay overnight, and be taken out when the child wants to go into the chamber (i.e. go to bed). (This implies a temporary solution to prevent re-blocking of the baby's fundament)
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And if this blockage comes suddenly of a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary to cover that suddenness: and let it be treated, just as we have said of the linen plug. (This implies a more serious condition requiring additional treatment)
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament (This suggests a specific medical condition being discussed)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas which come from under the fundament are constrictions, and grow larger when they come from below the fundament outside, or in the interval between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when that constriction is old, it works, and a moist grey or subtle whitish crust forms, and sometimes these fistulas heal; and are known by those things which issue or flow out of them or by their ventosity when the patient makes egestion, and perhaps a worm comes out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if it has fistulas that pierce just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis; and reach just to the junction of the vulva, and just to the edge of the knee. (This describes a specific type of fistula with multiple openings)
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula to be present at the fundament, and not present: and it is that you press your first finger or finger tip against the fundament, and push a fine needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is twisting, then I push in a thin tent of cloth or horsehair until you feel the tent or hair at your thumb; and if you don't feel it, and it doesn't come out with purging or ventosity or worm, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so do not hasten to treat.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula bursts open just to the bladder or just to the urinary canal, it lets out urine, and cannot be closed by medications. (This implies a severe condition where the fistula is causing a continuous leak of urine)
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced just to the joint of the groin, then the tent comes out at the place; if there is no twisting and the appearance of pain around, it is that it has gone through quickly, and it does not help medicine or ointment by anointing; and in these fistulas that pierce there is no cure other than surgery, and vanity of foolish surgeons who interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that which is not piercing and not ancient, has hope of healing by iron, so I have tried it, and the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lifts his legs up to his thighs, and inclines his thighs towards his belly; then insert a tent of lead, or of linen if there is tortuosity, as long as you know that the tent touches.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you should insert your two fingers there, and if at once the tent has pierced it; and be discovered where you feel between your finger the syphilis or the flesh, then know that it is piercing; if not to intervene because one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One always says that one can heal some, but it happens rarely; and the aid that we do there, is to heat the cautery finely according to the width of the fistula, as it was said before; and put it all hot in the fistula, until it comes near the fundament; and make this two or three times, as long as you know that those charred particles are burned, which resemble a bird's feather; and then cure with moist tented burrs, until those charred particles issue forth; then cure with ointment containing running flesh and soothing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus cleansed, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	Since that, otherwise it cannot be cleansed; and if the tent is inserted, but does not pierce right to the bottom which is at the foundation, and there is a thick covering of flesh or fat between your thumb and the tent, and you see the fistula through the covering of the wound; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push it immediately before the tent, and afterwards apply the cautery until it reaches the tip of the tent; and the tent will be delivered and dry; then scrape off those bad flesh bits that look like a bird's feather, and leave nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the scar comes back, and forms a bond between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicinal sharpness. (This describes a possible complication of the treatment)
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the cauterization of fire assembles two things: to wit, the charring of those stuck flesh bits, and the drying of blood and moisture; then treat damp tented wounds in mire or in a hot pit so that the sore ejects pus, and let the charred flesh come out into the pus; then treat the wound with ointments of sizzling onions to dissolve hard flesh, and those are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it will be healed and will not come back again. (This suggests that with proper treatment, the condition can be effectively managed and prevented from recurring)
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes just to the bottom of the fundament and is far from the body, then insert your finger or fundament, and investigate further. (This implies a need for closer examination or exploration of the area)
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the lump and it is between two places where there is a thread or sinew, or it is close to bursting through, so that you see only a sign of hope and promise, by the administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut into it just to the depth, or if you can put in tents and cure it as first; and don't go too deep, lest you cut the tendon that holds the foundation, and cause damage by unintentional movement; then cure it, as we have said. Perhaps it will be healed, or you remove the covering and clean it, since it has been cut next to the foundation, either with a probe or another instrument assigned: then cleanse the bad flesh that is in the wound, as long as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part beyond the foundation: if it were an easier thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And at any time are fistulas made in this manner: and is when you prick the tent in the fistula, and it is on one side of the foundation next to the skin above, then take a pricked tent at the head in this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put one. I. cord twisted in two, and plug the tent into all the string in the fistula as long as it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	She is pierced in the margin of the foundation within, then draw out the thread from that perforated one, just as you prick your thumb or the foundation; and pull the end of the thread, and tie the two ends together, and hold one against the other, and let it be for one day or two; and hold it once again, until the threads break through the flesh that is between them, and discharge; then treat the wound until it is sown up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in every way that you can, unless it is too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because it is not necessary to pierce through the thickening that has formed if it is too deep inside, and then heal it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spine from which one makes the fistula is very much curved on one side and blunt; and on the other side not at all, for this reason one does not pierce those things that one should not pierce, as you see here:
des emorroydes	the blood vessels
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorroids are according to II manners: or they are inside the fundament, such as grains of resin, and there are small ones and great ones, and in the court there is blood, and there is one or more, and are outside the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those which are outside so have a lot of moisture, and in the court there is either a drop of citrine water or a drop of blood, and have the color of flesh; and the cure for those who have them inside the fundament, it is that you command the patient to take purging potion in order to loosen in chambers until the fundament lets him come out, and so appears the filth; if you hasten, and hold with tweezers, or you hold at your fingernail, then cut in their roots; and if the hemorrhoids cannot be held for their moistors, take them up in a cloth, or in cotton, or in a piece of camlet; and draw out to thy hands, then cut, and powder above some hot powders that are in place of cautery; or you cauterize them as is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure with other cures until they be whole; and if the fundament cannot come out, clisterize the patient with clistere biting and harsh to wash what is inside the fundament, so that it can come out openly; for when the patient feels it, and the filth comes out from the fundament, then is the cure easy; and it is that you grasp them at your fingernail or with tweezers, and cut, then cure as we have said, until they be whole, and so avoid the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you bring the stitch according to this manner: take a twisted thread, and insert it into a needle, and then draw the thread upwards and make the needle pierce on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, so that they are of equal width; and hold the thread firmly, then bind the thread, and pull out the needle, and do the same for all the others, and leave it to bleed for a little while, letting go the superfluity of blood; then put on the bottom a damp cloth moistened in rose oil or cerote, and place it on the bottom, and instruct the patient to rest; and then let him be until he has stopped bleeding, and when they have fallen, treat them with ointment and other cures, so that he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the dryness of the fundament.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It often happens that there is dryness of the fundament in the intestine, and by natural constriction, and when the disease is old and medicine doesn't help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you reset a blister on the tip of a spavin or at your nail where the scab is above and does not let it moisten; then treat it until it is hardened as may be necessary; and if it cannot harden, then re-scrape more strongly than before, until it heals completely and is scabbed over; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	from the fistula.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A small false appearance appears around the body, and it goes very deep; sometimes the frost finds it, and one feels it just like a dead pulse, and it comes into all of the body, and more so in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a quill from a goose's feather or a strong turkey feather, and put that quill on the pulse, so long as the purple circles appear all around it; then turn your hand completely around the whole quill until it goes deep into the pulse, and remove the pulse from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that it's necessary, then make one from a piece of iron or steel in this form, and make it thin underneath and draw it upwards.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	don't make a hole, so that it can be held in the hand, and squeezed; and if you see fit, then cauterize the furuncle, as is said before or in the treatise on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	from the form of the clyster (enema).
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a clyster of silver or gold, or molten iron or linen, and sometimes one makes these instruments small and large, according to the form in which they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are made for the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large clyster is above wide or the belly is joined in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a rupture or the belly is bound together, as you see, and the head is pierced inside; and it has two perforations on one side, and one on the other; and the belly or womb is wrapped in medicines from an animal bladder or parchment, and is pierced all around with small perforations, and there are three threads of strong thread twisted into X's or crosses between each perforation; then tie up the belly like a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it with a strong string in front; then purify it.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the poultice with oil or hen's egg fat, or similar thing, then put it on lightly; then grasp the poultice with both hands together until it is completely wet, then remove the poultice, and raise the patient's legs to the bed, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it ooze so much as it can; and if it stays overnight altogether, it will be a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you have cleansed him with a syringe in the disease of obstruction of the belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are on the fundament or abscess, let the poultice be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of a subtle poultice on which the skin should be tightened:
des plaies	of sores
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will say about the treatments of hands and of medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or locations where the wounds are made, and of what kind they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the striking of a stone and cutting with sword and knife, or lance or staff or arrow, or similar things; or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that strikes on the neck, or on the head, or the breast, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a stone or similar things striking down, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt slightly of hot abscess: if so, treat the wound with cephalic remedy immediately even if blood flows from the wound, and the treatment be contrary to the injured part; and order the patient to drink wine and eat heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to heal, reduce his food and do not have him drink wine or eat meat; and put on the wound a poultice if hot abscess comes, with moistened cotton in rose oil alone, or in spirit of wine; and if there is no hot abscess, if you place on the wound, if it is fresh to all its blood, and it has not been moved by air, powder which I will tell about later; and if the fire has moved it, put on some ointments until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot join together by themselves, then assemble them with stitches, just as I will say about belly wounds, in the chapter on stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is uncovered to the bone and it can be held together with only a small amount of flesh, sew it up; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard skin in place of soft skin, and instruct the patient to eat large amounts of meat, such as cooked brains and wheat, also like fowl, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a rotting of the skin and it is not at the bone, sew up the rotting completely, and pour in pus, then treat it; and if there are arteries in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicine, tie the artery, and if you find it loose, tie it with a thread; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light, and it's that you put this powder on them, which heals even when the air has moved in.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method for this powder is: take one part of incense; dragon's blood two parts; and living gum three parts, and grind it finely, and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly until it is well closed and joins with all its blood; and then bind it tightly, and let it be without untying, if it does not become swollen; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one makes this medicine only of galena, when there is no frankincense or dragon's blood, but the air has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer has moved the wound, just as it is, then put no more of this powder on it; but lay some ointments digested, or dough made from barley flour with water and honey, so that it drips juice; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the break of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine tweezers; and I will tell you about the breaks of the head afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the jugular vein or artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, then leave no other treatment except to let it cure, and put nothing constricting on it, for it harms the nerves and causes them to retreat; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but if medicine is strong, such as soap washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and chamomile washed also in sweet water, and other herbal powders similarly, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then stitch it up with bandages, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and full of blood, pierce or lower in place; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding occurs, stop it, tie it, and cauterize it as needed; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the jugular vein, and keep the conduit by which the flesh goes, stitch up the wound on the skin of the neck, and do not touch the throat but place it according to its natural shape; and then bind it gradually, and leave it for a while, then cure with unguents that have been made in such a way until they are healed; and if the wound has depressed into the bone, probe it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove all you can, and what you cannot take out, let alone until the wound suppurates and is closed and clean the issue; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle powder on it that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has formed an abscess, then treat it as I said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of wounds caused by a spear or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's a blow from a lance or sword, and the wound is deep, see if there is windiness coming from the wound in the direction that the patient shivers: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it's not deep, and it's fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it for the sake of the blood that may not dry thoroughly, and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but put attractive ointment on it, and bind it twice a day; and if you don't have ointment, put old cloth in the wound to soak up moisture, and make the patient sleep above the wound three days, or four, or more; then there will not come spasms, nor bad trembling of the heart or straining of limbs; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the patient with tents and other treatments until they are healed; and if they cannot heal and recover, then know that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut of sword or knife and is simple, or worse on the front, or back, treat it with what is in front; if it's large, sew it up; and if it's small, powder it; and if it has gotten into the bone and there are splintered pieces, clean the wound and pull out any foreign objects that have entered; and if they haven't entered, let the wound rot until it will help with extraction; and for other wounds in other limbs use the same judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the bursting of the belly.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The ruptures of the belly are great and middle-sized and small; from the large wound the intestines or the membranes of the intestines sometimes burst out with it; and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worth less than a big one, for that's why we put the intestines in gently when we don't put them in hot to hot; because the intestines swell right away when they feel cold, so they go back in more easily, and therefore a middle-sized wound is worse, for this reason we mend the intestine to its place before other two And know that the rupture of the belly occurs in four ways: the common stitches occur in the stitching of the belly, and the stitches of other wounds of the body are two others common to other wounds; but nonetheless they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will say each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and some thing from the intestines has issued forth, and a grievous thing must be done, it is done in one of two ways: or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, heat it in this manner: soak a sponge or a cloth of wool in hot water just to the touch, or cook in hot water with cypress and spike, and wrap the intestine so that the swelling is removed; and once you have done this, hold it back in place and be careful not to swell again.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling departing, if you moisten the intestine with water or wine and spices are cooked, for by that is relieved the opening to a small part; and if it cannot enter, make a small pouch of the wound with the instrument with which one clips hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to sew up, so that none should cut without great necessity having; and this is the instrument to split it: so cut from inside in the shape and not outward, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is swollen and the intestines have burst forth, put it back in place according to its natural form into its proper location, if you are able, for this is a movement.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and it is in the lower part of the belly, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, place the head and chest higher than the lower parts, and similarly so that the wound of the belly is in one of the two parts, place your intention so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to remember what I say in large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	Smaller wounds put what is closest to you, then take between your hands the holy oil that anoints all the wound with its hand, and gather the edges; and this is the common way of sewing, which is for you to take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the largeness of the wound, then leave the head of the wound two fingers' space, and insert a needle where there is good strong thread; and pierce the two holes of the skin with the two holes of the syphac, which is under the skin within, until you make it pierce from that part, and gather the two heads of the syphac together; then tie around the needle with a double thread for two parts, then gather the two edges of the wound together properly, and then leave two fingers' space, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to the need of the needles, until all the wound is restrained; and the needles should be moderate, between fine and coarse, for the fine needles pierce through all the flesh, and the too coarse ones cannot enter well: therefore it is necessary that they are moderate; and it is not necessary to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and open the wound in front of the suture; then cut off the heads of the needles, so they do not hurt the patient while sleeping, and put thread or cloth on the heads of the needles to keep them from moving, and leave them until the wound is sewn up; and this way of sewing with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because it only takes one needle or two The second suture is common, which is for you to gather the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the syphac together on a needle where there is a strong thread in middle; and when you have pierced these holes all four together, then withdraw the needle from the part where you began, in the manner that one sews clothes; and leave space between each suture the width of a small finger; this suture is known to men, and I sewed a wound which was on a man's belly, who had been injured by a knife, and the wound was more than a hand's palm large, and there were intestines damaged two hands' palms long, and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought him back his intestines after he had been without them for twenty-four hours; and the wound was sewn up until fifteen days, and I cured him, and he healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the barber had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in a place where one could not find any, nor any medicine; and I placed clean linen on the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until he healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and pass it through from outside to inside as far as it can go; when it has pierced the leather (or whatever is being sewn) straight through, then place the head of the thread or suture where you have passed in the needle, and make it pierce again from the inside to the outside as far as it can go; and the understanding of this suturing is that you sew just like a tailor does buttons, and leave once the thread on one side and take it up on the other, until the suture is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of stitching, which the Greeks call properly, is as follows: they bring together the two parts in a natural way and apply one of the ends of the thread to the other end, in this way: insert a needle or the tip of the thread near it, and make it perforate only that place, and leave the two ends of the thread; then turn the needle, and make it perforate from the outer part just up to the inner one at the two ends of the thread; then make each one perforate from the outer part just up to the inner one in two other holes of the thread which are on the opposite side; and this is the more secure manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Greeks say this saying, and some witness it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each; and one must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew seams; and know that when the tear is within the belly, then the stitch is more grievous than at other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as those of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, just as the fire has changed it, so put back the intestine, and the gut; then lay on powdering charcoal dust, and if the fire has changed it, lay on any ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and sew the skin, and suture the muscles, and the sinew; then cure the wound as with others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, put on, as soon as it begins to heal, old cotton, and move it two times a day, until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have need of no other medicine in many simple conditions for the wounds; and if you doubt that the wound will make community with the principal members, it is necessary that you soak linen lightly in tempered hot oil, or rose oil, and put it around the angles, and under the armpits; and if he feels pain or purge in the bowels, and many times has, then cleanse with black wine vinegar, and similarly if the purging comes just to the intestine; and puncture within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is more easy to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeun" cannot heal when they are injured, and this is because of the bloated veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the approaching of its nature to the navel.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the sutures fall from the wound, then put them back again as fresh as the intestines; and if they are old and have turned green or black, you must tie the place that is black so that no blood comes out because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligature, and let the two ends hang from the part underneath the wound right up to the outside in order to lighten the extraction when the sutures fall, and the wound swells.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bowel.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, one can sometimes restore it in some people, because I have seen a man injured with a lance to the stomach; and the wound was on the right side of the abdomen, and became inflamed and turned into an abscess, and from which there was discharge and flatulence; I put treatment according to what I knew, and did not cease to apply gentle care until he was healed, and the tear sealed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewed, I doubted that the patient would have an illness in his belly; and there was no illness, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking; and some experimentors said that when it has a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in this manner: take a large thread, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened the mouth, place it on the two lips, so that it closes its mouth above; and then hit the head, and it holds as long as it cannot untie it, then put another thread after in this way as before, until the wound is completely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	That thread if it is sewn in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that has been scraped from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the head of this thread of intestine that has been very well cleaned, and then tie to the head of this thread a fine linen thread twisted, then push the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and sew it back up; and this way of sewing with thread is no other than according to the path of trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the folds of the intestines, there is no remedy or cure, unless subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be;
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it festers, is commonly called a "fistula", and likewise when it breaks out and runs below.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to its greenish nodulated formation firm and bluish, where one does not feel pain, and it is also running like the feather of a bird; and sometimes it runs clear below, and at other times thick; at times it dries up, and at other times it is quite full; and I have spoken elsewhere in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is due to one of the nine causes: that is to say, by the thinness of blood or body; or because of its malicious nature; or because there is hard flesh inside and above the lips, and does not let new flesh grow; or there is too much discharge; or the site is corrupted, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in treatment; or because the corruption is a manner of plague; or because of the property in the region is slow digestion, and delays healing, and tends by nature to fester; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines elsewhere in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is fitting that I should tell you the treatment for a fistula, which is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	There are fistulas that occur in all the members of the body; for they arise in great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or in the skin, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet; and such that come to the principal property of the member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous healing, and there is no other remedy than surgery, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come right to the place that I said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it known, then take a tent made of lead or iron, if the fistula is straight, seek it out; and if the fistula is crooked, seek it with a subtle tent of plonc, because the plons bend around the tortuousness; and if the fistula has many perforations and you cannot well probe it with tents, then cleanse it through one of the perforations, for the moisture flows from one perforation to another, and cleanses it; then lance it according to your power, knowing if there is bone or nerve, and if it is deep inside, and ask the patient clearly about the pain he feels when pressing your hand on it, and where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or from a nerve, or from an artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the evil formation and the corrupted cartilage that are inside; and then cure it as long as it is healed, and if the fistula is well-deepened in a straight place, then you must cut deeper, so much as you can, then put moist tents with medicated water in them, into the chief of the fistula, so much as the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then put ointments on green flesh so long as they are healed; and if it is not healed by those means, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve does not grieve or harm the principal member, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then clear it out so that all the corruption is removed, then cure with a thing drawing out blood so long as they are healed; and if they are not healed, and return to its former condition, know that you have not gone far enough: clear and dig until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	Know that if not, know that the corruption is too deep and you cannot approach it: if there is no other remedy than to leave nature; and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can draw it out with pincers, then pull it out with an instrument suitable for this, and if there are many bones, then draw them all out, leaving none behind; and if the moisture makes it difficult, and there is no mistake or fear, then cut and remove the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, so place on the wound a thing inducing putridity, and let it be such that the place around the bones is putrid; and then they will have bones more easily set; and if it is a great bone, such as of leg or thigh, see only the corruption until all blackness is gone, then restore the wound; and if there is great part of corrupted flesh, and comes just to the edge of the bone; so you must clean and cover everything just to the corruption, and then heal them until they are sound; and I will tell you about a fistula which occurred in a man's leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came within the body, so that the materials went to the leg, and he had a large abscess, and did not have an external cause to open it; but the physicians through their foolishness worked on it so much that the abscess opened, and they caused much material to come out, and it became a fistula, and there came out many holes from which all sorts of foul-smelling and moist things were discharged; and many physicians placed treatment around 2 years, and there was no wise person in the art of healing, until I was called to it, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they treated him, and what was coming out through the holes, a large quantity; and the body of the young man became red and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that one comes against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried then, and cut into one of the holes as far as I uncovered a part of the bone, and I found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption came up to the bone inside; I removed what appeared from the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption, except for what I had already removed; and I began to treat the wound with soothings for a long time, but could not heal it; and then I started again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then I tried to repair the place; but I couldn't do so until I cut around a palm's length of the bone, and pulled it further all the way around, then treated it with medicines; and it healed quickly and was made whole, and there was no need to start again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and because of my fear of his death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because the evacuation [of blood] would often cause bleeding, but he was completely cured, and in place of the bone there grew a hard skin, and he had good disposition and did not have any harm or contraindication at all, neither for eating nor for coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it must be sewn up in this way: take a thread and stretch it at the head of the bone which is open, and command someone to hold it upright; and take another thread of linen larger than the first thread, and tie it on the skin that is above the bone, so that you draw out the corrupt flesh below, and uncover the skin on the place where you see that it can be sewn, without wounding the skin; and put a hot iron or a flat piece of wood under the bone to cover the corrupt flesh; and it must be sewn as much as can be seen and felt the corruption, and also sewn again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then reveal all the flesh; then put hot coals beneath, and then draw out the corruption from one part to another, and be sure that the instrument will reach the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut off the corrupted joint, and draw out the bone where it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the connection of two joints, then there is no other remedy but to cut; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand, or in the heel of the foot, then this thing is very strong, but nonetheless you must investigate that corrosion how it presents itself; and purify it in all the ways that you can, but do not let the sinew or nerve be against you; and know that the instrument and threads for cutting these bones are many, according to the shape of the bone and its appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each likeness of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of illnesses; so think about the instrument which you have need of, according to what it is fitting.
dou feu	from fire. (a return to a more poetic tone)
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The body parts can be corrupted either from inside or from outside; and when you will have medicined that corruption with the cure of medicines, and they do not profit, then it is necessary to cut off that member up to the place where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes by this means from death, or from the greater evil, the loss of the member; and the signs are such that the member becomes black, so that it seems to have been burnt by fire, and after the blackness, that corrosion spreads from member to member, and takes throughout the body; if you hasten to cut off, and this is due to the bite of certain venomous beasts, as scorpion of the sea and viper and similar, then if the corruption is in the head of the arm, cut it off, and do not give him space for it to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, then cut off at the joint, so that the corruption does not come up to the arm; and if it comes into the arm, then cut off at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy other than the quantity of its virtue; and do thus also when the corruption comes to the foot: if it comes in the first joint, then cut off after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, then cut off the whole foot; and if it mounts up into the leg, then cut off at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy but that the patient will die; and the manner of cutting or sewing the member is such that you tie him on top and underneath, and stretch out one servant of the string down, and another servant of the string up, and you loosen the flesh which is between the two strings a wide spatula, so that the bone is uncovered; then cut off or sew, and put linen cloth on each side so that the stitching does not touch the healthy place, and the patient will come to other lesion and swelling afterwards.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.
