And if bleeding occurs from the cut when you work, cauterize the place at once with some binding powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to that man in my village: he had a burn that seemed like coal fire, and that burn came first on his right foot, so much that it consumed all of the foot; and when the man saw the burn, he hastened to cover his foot, and was healed; and long after him, the same burn came back on his hand, and he came to me, and I put some rebounding things on him after the purifying of the body, and he could not stop the burn; and he asked that I cut off his hand, and I did not want to, for I had hope of rebounding the material; and I also doubted if I would cut off his hand, that he would die, for the virtues of the man were weak; and he became desperate completely, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; and I have not yet told this story except in order to do something else.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	At some time an abscess forms in a fatty place, and remains so long that it makes a large collection of pus; and then bursts and opens, and the body's skin is left empty, just like worn-out cloth. And the skin that is on top is also very fine like delicate fabric, and they do not break down just to the bone or just to the nerve, and such a disease is called "sinus", and it is not called "fistula"; but if it becomes so long that it comes to the bone inside deeply, then it is called "fistula"; and the treatment is that you cut off that skin all around, and in particular when it is fine like fabric; and they are not operated on because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you suspect that the skin is corrupting and the corruption is not deep inside, and the skin is thick with fat, then cure it with a clyster thus: look to see if the breast is large, and the abscess which is within it has foul odor, then make the Egyptian medicine for it thus: take ashes, oil, and lye, equally, and put them in a vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red, and thickens like honey; and then take some of it according to your need, and make it into water and honey, and cleanse the breast with it, and stop up the hole; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by pressing out; do this many times, until the breast is clean and free from foulness; and sometimes a clyster of ashwater is used, when that medicine is not present, and that you take ashes from grapevine wood, and pour water over them, then let it cool, and cleanse with it, as long as you know the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot endure it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor the ashwater, then cure it with water and honey or it has a drop of lye in it; or you will clyster it with honey and sweet wine, that the honey may have the property to cleanse and wash, and the wine may make the discharge warm; and when you have done this, and suspect that the breast is well cleansed, then cure it with things that cause flesh to grow within it, and that you take diaphane powder, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or you will clyster it with some medicines and ointments, of which I said the properties in treating ointments; and if the hole of the breast is small, and the clyster cannot enter it, then enlarge it with a iron point, and put on a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, as long as it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then cut around it and leave just enough for the clyster to enter, and if the abscess that flows pus is above, then stop up the hole higher or lower than where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the boil is in its depth, do not let it send forth pus; and if you cannot cover the breast from below as you see, prepare in such a manner that the boil runs to the lowest place it can, for when the boil is deep, do not let it send forth pus and if you cannot cover the breast from below as you see, prepare in this way: that the boil runs lightly downwards and let nothing of the boil remain; and take consolidating medicines to put on the skin, and are on the linen cloth that covers all the skin; then cut at the strongest point the nipple of the breast a little larger than the first, afterwards anoint with soft ointment on the other cloth according to the quantity of the pustule, and put it on the pustule of the skin to loosen the boil, and do not remove the large cloth outside which after many days once; and that which is on the pustule of the breast, remove often to remove the boil, and know what escapes from the boil, if it is venom or pus or enough, or digestible, or indigestible; and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has thus spread and you see the nature that comes on the pustule of the skin, then know that the breast is averted, and approaches health; and then untie it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you untie the wound, then change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast continues to discharge undigested pus after many days, know that the breast has not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons cut through after a long time, do not lose hope of health, for the patient is approaching recovery.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people who suffer a long time with pus in their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if indigestible matter bursts out from under the skin after many days, know that the body is not healing; and if the abscess delays to form and grows hard, take medicines of dry substances and dry virtues, such as clarified ointment, for it contains a great part of vitriol, and it is the last medicine; take clarified ointment, and mix it with rosated oil, and rose petals in equal substance; then cook and use it; and do the same thing with honey that has been cooked and thickened, when clarified ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and pound them, and powder them over the honey when it is on the fire; then apply a cloth soaked in it to the chest, and at some point administer old Aristolochia longa, and roots of lily flower, which is also like flour from vetches and centaury; and use either simples or compounds: pound them, and make powder, and put it over the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if the treatment is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment, then know that corruption has sunk in deep, and made a breach in the bone, or in hard members, or in sinews; so apply the cure for fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the suppurating boil.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is a swelling that arises under the nail of the hand or foot, or by chance in other places; and when it becomes hardened, and one does not take care of it, then the swelling bursts and flows with pus as long as there are vessels within the swelling to carry it; and possibly even breaks through completely; and comes a corruption right up to the bone, causing a foul pain, and the joint of the finger is large, and the color is darkened.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut off completely all the excess tissue that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a very great aid if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; but if the nail presses against the flesh, starts to throb, and becomes inflamed, then you must put hot oil under the nail that throbs against the flesh, pour it upwards, and cut off that sensitive flesh carefully and lightly, and apply on the remaining flesh medicines burning and corrosive so as to remove all of it; then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut it out and remove the tumor, because as long as the bone is corrupted within it cannot heal; and if you see that the marrow is corrupting, then cut into the bone from below just as is said before, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is festering and suppurating, and it causes great pain, then you must first clean it; afterwards cut the angle of the spatula in a slanting manner above, and be careful that the blade does not reach all the way to the flesh which is under the bone, because the patient would feel too great pain; and if it happens, place something on top which soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the abscess in the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The swellings that arise in the hands of some men by chance are entirely fleshy, and sometimes there is a lump where there should be bones, and at times it has an angle, and some of them grow in the root of the joint, or the growth is in certain parts of the marrow of the bones.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born without any defect in the knee does not move, and he who is born with the joint of the knee has a chance to move; the height of one who is fat is light, in the same way: cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who occurs in the root of the joint is hard to cure, and you must hold on to cutting.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For he who is born or should be near the rear wound, it is necessary that you cut around the flesh up to the bone first, then cut the bone with a string suitable for this, then heal it until it is sound.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The burn or scald that comes to the hands together comes from birth, or a wound, or a burn of fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut the conjoined wound so that it can be repaired according to its natural forms; then put between two tents or wetted cloths in rose oil, so they do not join together; or put between two thin pieces of linen, until the place is joined, as it is required.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If scalding comes to any of his hands with the palm, then cut out that scalded area as it is necessary.
des vils	bad things
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Swollen veins are thickened and enveloped, full of superfluous melancholy substances, which come to many members of the body; and there is more in legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	So it is necessary that you administer them sometimes an evacuation of gall and then cleanse with the white of egg.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of iron is according to two manners: one is that you cut it, and then draw out the black blood; and the other manner is that you tie a vein, and then strip it all through.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting is according to this manner: first take the leg of sharp hot water very strong, until the thick blood is thinned out; then bind the patient's leg above the knee just up to the part below the kneecap; then cut the vein in one place, or in two, or in three, with a broad cut; then lift and draw out the black blood from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient can endure; and then bind it back, and command him that he should become pale eating greasy cold meat; and repeat the evacuation and washing when the veins are full, and harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Loose the skin of the leg from the patient, if there is much hair; then put it in a bath, and take the leg with hot iron until it becomes red and swollen; and if you do not have a bath, heat it over the fire, and then soak the area around the vein at the knee or just below the ankle; then loosen the skin with a needle, and scrape the vein from each side until it is apparent when one feels it; and it looks red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then push in stitches as much as the skin allows, and then tie them lightly, then soak the area around the vein at another knot three times; then scrape the skin over the vein until it is apparent, then raise it to the iron, just as you have done, and soak it in another knot, just as you have done first; then make an incision or more if necessary, then lift it, and cut at the foot of the ankle, then pull out and lift up to the second incision; then pull it from incision to incision until it is completely freed, then cut it; and if you cannot pull it out and lift it, insert a needle into every double thread strong thread and tie and pull, and put stitches under the iron, and turn your hand from one side to the other until something comes out; and be careful that it does not tear, because if it tears, it can no longer be pulled out or lifted, and it will harm the patient; and when you have completely pulled it out, then apply wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the area of the wound, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and entwined together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it lengthwise, but do not cover it; and treat it in the manner that we have previously described.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron with which one covers a vein is curved, and does not cut it, lest one cuts the vein; and is of great curvature, for if it were thin, one would pierce the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot parts where neither herbs nor trees grow, and on dry land where there is no moisture; and it may also be located elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens because of the corruption that comes from under the skin, as snakes and worms come inside the body and are embedded between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein so are that it comes to the leg a great inflammation, then it changes its place, and the vein begins to come out, just as the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein has been opened, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth one and a half hands long up to two hands, and the node, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it becomes pointed at its end, you wrap it around the cloth and the node; and if it is too long, you cut off a part of it, and wrap the remaining part around it, and do not cut it in its root until it has come out completely; because if you cut it, it goes back into the flesh and causes an abscess and putridity at the place, and a bad disease; for this reason it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the end, and none remains in the body; and sometimes this vein when it has been treated two hands long, or ten, and I have seen one come out nine hands long, and when you cut it, it spouts a fistula or a perforation, and it must be pierced right down until everything comes out; and the material that is inside is emptied, and medicines are given to the place for three days to prevent putridity, then it cures just like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And any time this vein is cut open, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or the foot itself, or there are many pores, and from which rain flows; then cure it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "disease of the ox", because it has often happened to cows, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body rising and descending, and feels them very well from limb to limb, until it breaks through the skin where it goes, and makes a boil; and it is engendered by corruption of some humors, as come worms and serpents and lice and tapeworms in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps enters, and destroys the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cured and healed, one cannot be sure that it will not recur: so then you must bind the area above and below with a strong string tightly, then incise on top and remove the abscess, and if the pus is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize with fire on top until it boils; and the greatest harm that it does is that it will corrode the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or chief near the eye, then restrain below it the eyelid firmly, then incise on top, and remove the abscess; and it is necessary to use the patient with cleansing of body medicines soluble for bad humors and unhealthy foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from wind (or vertigo)
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and it moves from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; and afterwards, I saw it rise as quickly as a worm on the shoulder, as sharp as silver when it cuts from one place to another; the pain moved away from that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then a little while after it spread throughout the body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it kept rotating around the body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved from member to member in this way, for I had never seen that disease behave in this manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had often seen that the pain moved from one place to another, but I did not see it in this way with the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins were uncovered, and for this reason the swelling appeared constrained; and they do not appear according to this reason in those who are fat, and have moist bodies and closed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said, then tie a bandage above and below hastily; and then prick on top until the swelling is constrained back into place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see improvement with your eyes, then cure with those who are skilled in treating swellings, such as fetid pills, and serpent pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	from arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their kinds is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and barbed, and feathered; and those with two angles, and those with shafts, and those with pieces; and the one which lodges in any member so lodges in two ways: or it pierces a principal member, such as brain, heart, liver, intestines, kidneys, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls into some place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears to you: so you must beware of extracting this arrow, for many die afterwards in various dispositions; and when this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes and penetrates the bone, and bursts the scull that is above the brain, is when there are scotoma and sode and esvertin and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and perplexity of understanding, and vomiting of gall; and perhaps it falters from the nostrils, or the ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice; and there is a moist white discharge from the wound, resembling boils, and also like charred flesh; and if this sign appears to you, then beware of treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the stone when it falls into the heart are that it is close to the left breast, and feels as though it were stuck in a hard thing, not empty; and perchance the stone moves like hairs, and in dark red blood, and comes with cold sweat, and fainting: know then without doubt that the patient will die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the arrow that never lodges in the navel are: there is a foaming discharge coming out of the wound, and the throat swells up, and the sick person changes color, and sighs loudly and asks for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow lodges in the covering of the liver, it is located near the small ribs; and there is a great pain and a great agony, and the sick person sighs; and the muscles of all the members of the shoulders are convulsed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow lodges in the stomach, perhaps something from the undigested meat comes out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow lodges in the abdomen and there is no passing of feces through the rectum, then there is no hope for a cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow lodges in the bladder, and urine comes out and flows away, and the sick person feels a great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, arms, neck, shoulders, and armpits, and the spine of the back, and the ribs, and the hips, and the thighs, and similar members, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and it is venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	An arrowhead fell into the corner of a man's eye in the root of his nose; I attempted to remove it and pulled it out from the other side under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out an arrow that had fallen into the fat of a man's eye under the parchment there, and the arrow was bent back, and I could only grasp its tip towards the handle, and the arrow was as long as a Turkish bow, made entirely of iron without any handles; the patient was healed, and no evil accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And drew out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic to the ears: I shaved the fletching, and whittled it so much that I could draw it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And drew out an arrow from his home, which was stuck in his belly, and thought he would die; and then that it had passed 30 days, and its condition did not change; I cut above the arrow, and bound him, and pulled it out, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see the man to whom an arrow struck in the back, and the wound was healed above; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change its natural condition, nor caused any harm to one of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you see another man, to whom an arrow struck in his face, and the wound was healed; and he remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated an arrow that had pierced the king's thigh, which was stuck in the bone, and it was slightly leaning to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded. I was called to treat him three days after it had been pierced.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I searched for it with a fine needle and did not feel it at all; and he felt pain and discomfort under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow I put on top of it a poultice of attracting and digestive properties, so that the area would not become inflamed; and the shape of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put on a poultice for seven days and the wound closed again, and the patient remained in that state for a long time, until he felt the arrow the next day inside his bone; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I placed on the wound a medicinal paste made of corrosive substances by hand every day, until it was completely open, and I tried it, and felt the head of the arrow which was stuck in its place; then I inserted into the opening of the wound with that medicine, so that the head of the arrow appeared clearly to me; and it healed well around the terminus for IV months, and then burst out such a way that I put tongs on it from one side and the other, and it could not come out; then I did not cease to refine and invent ways with instruments, until I took it out I day with tongs very well made, according to what its shape would come at the end of this chapter, so that I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the wise men judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you may apply your treatment to what I am not saying; for the books cannot take everything in; but wise masters compile a great little thing and a present and failing thing, new work and new instrument, at the descent of strange things which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come out of members or go in except in two ways: either through the place where they enter, or on the other side; and that one which comes out by the place where it entered is an arrow entering into fleshy parts, and does so now and then.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, let it be left until the flesh is very swollen around it, and the issue has been cleared; and similarly if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, let it be left for some days, and each day try to move it; and then it will come out, and if it does not come out, make a small incision all around the point as subtle as can be, until the place around it is enlarged, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and I have mentioned some accidents that may happen to the patient: do not pull it out at all, but let it be as long as it is even after some days, because if the arrow comes close to the pituitary, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone itself and does not come to the pituitary, and the patient remains a few days without bad accident, then the instrument for pulling it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deeply stuck and cannot come out, I administer theriac around it, as I have told you before; then care for the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is returned to its place in the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it with a probe. And if you feel it, pull it out with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then enlarge the wound as much as possible; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if the arrow has ears to which it holds, remove the flesh that is stuck in place with two parts until you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow so that you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, so that you would draw it more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out at once, then leave it until the surrounding area is putrid, and then pull it out, for the extraction will be clearer.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If the bleeding from the cut makes you contrary, administer what we have said about the cure in its chapter; and beware of cutting into the nerve and vein, and know how to carefully draw out the arrow without danger, soon or late, strongly or gently; and put the patient back in the shape it was when the arrow hit him, for that is the greatest aid, and if you cannot, then do as the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another side, or it breaks off something of it, or the skin is inflamed in front where you can see or feel apparently: cut then above, as long as the forceps can take hold, and then pull it out; if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand around so that it goes into the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, then leave it and then resume extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, then push it all into the shaft; and if the shaft is broken, and you wish to administer poultice, then give the instrument pointed, so that the point of the arrow enters the hair of the instrument; and then push out, and if the arrow is barbed, then put the instrument in with entering point ahead, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow is embedded, you must cut out all the flesh around where the venom is, if possible, then treat the wound as it requires.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls into the back or side or belly or bladder or ribcage and is close to the surface and you can cut on top of it, cut there; and be careful not to cut the vein and nerve, then pull it out, and then sew up the wound as needed; and cure it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to pull out arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and see this form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many shapes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the feathers of a bird, in order to push against the tip of the arrow, as is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the forceps for inserting and checking if it's like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	arteries of the common body.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins by which one is healed are XXXI, of which there are XVI on the head, to wit: the two beating veins that are behind the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the two temples apparent; and the two veins that are in the two arches of the eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the neck; and the two jugular veins that are in the neck; and the two veins that are on the upper lips above the mouth, and they are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly used for bloodletting are V-shaped in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, and it is located on the left side; and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle vein is called "fistula", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins; and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is located on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly"; and it is above the elbow, and it is that one from which we bleed, which appears clearly on the forearm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the ring and the little finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is under the kneecap on the left side, and the second sapheneus which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called "popliteal" which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting from the veins that are behind the ears helps the cathartics of old and migraine; and the quality of a good bloodletter is such as I tell you, and it is to lift up the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with an astringent cloth; then bind the patient's neck with a cord until the two veins behind the ears appear in two dependent places near the head: then take your thumb, and press down on the pulse below your thumb, signifying to start. Then take the lancet, and insert it beside the vein up to the bone, then lift up your hand and cut through both the skin and the vein with a single stroke of the blade, and make the blood flow until you see; then bind and tie it tight until it is healed; and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is good to bleed a person who is old, and sick, and accustomed to ophthalmia, and in the eyes; and the quality of the bleeding is such as I say: and it is that the patient stretches his neck, so that the two veins appear openly; and feels the fold under your thumb, then signs with an incision; then raises the key on the vein up to your index finger, and inserts the lancet below, and raises the vein up, and clips it, as you have done in the other two veins, and makes a cut in the blood according to your need; then unbinds the patient, and puts your thumb on the vein an hour, then put on cotton; and then tie firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their closure and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding from the vein of the forehead is worth as much as the bleeding from the cerebral vessel in ancient facial diseases, and in migraine, and in headache; and the quality is that the patient strains his neck by twisting, so long as the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose shape is this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point above the vein, and press with your hand, or something else, and let two drops of blood come out according to the quantity you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein so that it is bound and at no time will the work be done by a large burning.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not advisable for the bandages to be too tight; and for the bloodletting to be done in such a way that it crosses over, because the bone is close by, and it may break through the bandage if it becomes too thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding from the two veins that are in the two eyelids is helpful to the eyes, and to the itch, and to the headache, and to the horiuel in the eye, and to facial diseases; and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient strains his neck by twisting with some thread, as before; then let it bleed, and the bleeding will be like the cutting through a piece long and thin of flame, one part of which is a bit narrow, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the bandages are thin, it may break through; then make a small incision in the blood, as much as you need, and then apply compresses on top of cotton, and tie them tightly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood from the vein of the neck is very valuable for ague and a sudden fever, and for facial diseases, such as migraine and eczema that comes in the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the blood is that the patient tightens their throat, then stretches their neck to your left hand, and takes the thin flame long, and puts it inside the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well in front, and the blood will start flowing now; do not go too far in depth, and let the blood flow according to your need, then tie it up for a night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood from the two great veins is helpful for the tightening of the throat, and the beginning of a boil, and many diseases, and atrophy, and corrosion, and herpes, and eczema; and the quality of the blood is that the patient tightens their neck under both [veins], as we have said; and let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat, then bleed the vein from long a little widely, then draw out the blood moderately, or so much as is necessary; then do it again in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and bind around the veins moderately, so that the patient does not choke; and leave him until morning, that the wound may be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the cleansing of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bloodletting from the veins of the upper lips is helpful for ulcers in the mouth, and for corruption of the gums, and fissures of the lips, and of the nape and throat.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of this cleansing are to have the patient sit in front of you, and hold their neck as I said; then turn back the lips, and look at the two veins, one being on the right lip and the other on the left, and they can be known by them being black, and because around them there are small black threads: cut therefore both and if you do not recognize them, and you have doubt, so cut the larger of each side; and do in the same manner to the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the cleansing under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The cleansing of the veins that are under the tongue is done after the cleansing of the cephalic, and it's for the constriction of the throat, and for eye diseases, and for mouth diseases; and the qualities of the cleanser are that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and they lift their tongue, and look under each edge at a black vein: cleanse therefore both and do not go too deep because there are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	Veins of the throat which are commonly treated are cured in two ways: or they pierce with a large flame-quenching myrrh, or an olive oil needle if you will, called "anesil"; and they are large and subtle according to the largeness and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the very large bandage is well-known, and it's wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the thick blood-filled veins that are plain and contain much blood and turmoil; and this is the form of the olive oil flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more fine-pointed, and it's used to bleed the thin veins, where there is fine yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilic, which is one of these veins, so helps with the diseases that are under the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the belly; and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed him carefully, and to beware of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he strikes the artery and a great flow of blood comes out, then he must stop it, as I have said; and he should not strike with the flame, but cut like anesil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not open obviously, you must extract it, and change to another; or you wish to take some blood from it, or you make a cut into the arm in its place: it opens obviously; and the ligature is applied to the flame with vinegar, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the location of the vein, then you must extract the arm, so that you touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the place with ink, and then bind the arm, and make a cut into the vein with vinegar flame; and beware that you do not strike in the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery: take your leave then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it come out as high as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood: hurry then, and put your finger above it for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind the arm, and leave it so, and do not move the patient; and be on guard, and do not move them until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped and it's urgent, and there are no remedies present, then cut the artery if it appears, because the head will pull back; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a rind of fig tree, and boil it, and take one half and tie it well up to the other joint; if the wound is clean, it's well; if not, cure it with the powders that stop blood as we have said; and the clotting is not very difficult in many conditions for the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm tendon.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The bloodletting of the vein in the middle so helps that it treats the blood from the head above, and from the body below, because it is composed of basilic vein and cephalic vein, as we have said; and the surgeon should beware for the nerve which is beneath, and if he pokes too deep and finds the nerve, and it swells and the bleeding becomes difficult, and by chance cannot heal; and this nerve opens up very often, and if it does not open in some people because of its subtlety, then you must stop the bleeding with the instrument anesil; and push aside the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there are veins between the two nerves, cut them long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bloodletting from the cephalic vein so helps, that it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; and one should bleed in puncturing with a flamed olive branch or a flamed myrtle twig, for this is the most safe of all the veins, since it has no nerve or artery underneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	In any case, one should seek the most lightweight position, and not harm anything if it is failed at first, and then try again; and perchance the places swell in some men when it is attempted for the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bloodletting is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding, is that bleeding is not made except to preserve health, and to avoid upcoming illnesses; and the bleeding is done in one of the three veins which are the neck: it is to say, cephalic, facial, and basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of March or July, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the sign of repletion becomes apparent; and one should bleed on the first day or third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The physician who administers the treatment to the sick has no fixed time determined, but when need arises during the day or night, at all hours and in all seasons; and it is not necessary to treat children until they are fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying fruit for more than seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should one be healed who has passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when some want to be treated, however it may be, then they must clear the intestines with a light catheter, if they have much foul matter retained, so that the veins do not draw out of the intestines the superfluous things that harm the main members; and they do not treat those who are too full of meat, nor those who are drunk, until they are sober, nor those who are dropsical; and warn them to be treated after a fit of colic, vomiting, and bowel trouble, and frequent intercourse with women, and work, vigilance, and sleep, and all that which is good for the body, or by something of arms or from the heart; then subtilize the humors, if the swelling is great, by meat and drink and medicines, if you have the power; then enter in water, if nothing prevents it, to subtilize the blood, and be treated for the pain around the stomach's third part, as we have said; and guard that day of work, and of labor, and of lust, and of similar things; and be happy and joyful, and let the physician be higher than those whom one treats, and wipe the arm two or three times, then loosen the string above gradually, for if it is too tight or loose, so the swelling cannot be corrected; and then rub the hands on the place where they want to treat, until the veins swell, and are felt; then moisten the physician's hand with the flame of an old oil; then put their right hand over that vein above the place where one wants to treat, so that the vein does not break or fail when being pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.
