There are veins that flee as swiftly as strings to the seamstress, and such ones that are full of windiness; so that when one puts on the flame, it recoils from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of these; and if the vein overflows, then the wound is too narrow, therefore the surgeon must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein bursts open at first time, that's good; if not, then he starts again a little below or above the same spot, as long as the skin is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the swelling is great, and the patient fears, let him be left for one or two days, and do not tie the arm down: perchance abscesses will form; don't get in the bath, but resume the treatment if it pleases you; and if the puncture is small, or the blood flow is subtle, and you doubt that it is not coming out as much blood as you see, then put the flame directly into that same puncture; and do this work hastily, so that the swelling will be great; for often times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the area swelled, do not re-start the incision again, and put on a small patch of linseed oil, because it lightens the body from blood, and the linseed oil is mixed in this swollen area; thus administer linseed oil to every incision that you make when opening veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing is done for triage and bowels of water, when it is put on the area; so subdue the swelling and let it separate when it becomes too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if it comes to a large abscess, which has happened many times, especially when the incision is not well sewn up or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put on the area a moist sponge in hot water and vinegar, and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the bleeding from the vein has stopped, and if there is any blackness or greenish color remaining at the site after some days, it will not harm; and if you see anything, put on something made of aloes or myrrh mixed with wine vinegar, verdigris, or similar things.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there has been an abscess and an appearance at the healing of the basilica: then put your hand on it, and if you find the spot soft to the pressure of the hand, it is that bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not put on anything of what we have said, for perhaps it will cut the artery's blood; but make a dry plaster to harden the spot, and then treat it with another treatment, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to its amount of blood and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	If the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it thins; and if it's too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for the one who is swollen and inflamed, and in need of blood extraction, that a larger wound be made, and the flaps be large; and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it should be healed slowly and often, and one should heal it by cutting at an angle, not by puncturing; and this manner of healing saves from hemorrhaging of blood and compression of nerve, and is better than long or wide incision.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for the one to whom the body is lacking in healing, it is necessary to give moistened bread dipped in juice of green apples; if he is hot-blooded, apply a poultice three or four times with blood; and if he has a cold complexion, moisten the bread before the wound with a sweet syrup, or with aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he spits up blood, after the emission of much blood, then it is necessary that he inhale a broth of flesh, and a subtle aromatic syrup, and use other things which we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to relieve his arm, and heal it again another time, when it is weakened by great bleeding, he should bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuing.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong pulse, should bleed 7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to be bled from another place, he should be bled on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For he has much blood inside the body which is already heated and brings on fever; so it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and enlarge the wound as far as it can open up; then you should reward all the conditions of spitting up blood, and put your hand on his shoulder when he spits up blood, so that death may not come in place of spitting up blood, and this happens many times, when the surgeon is careless; and it does not happen when you see him unfasten the arm, and let out blood a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press strongly on it; nor if it is crooked, that he stretch out his arm hastily, for it would be bad; but leave it until he spits up blood a second time; or you prick at the tip of the flame, as long as the congealed blood which has issued from the wound flows out, and put on a poultice made with silk soaked in water, and press on it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it again, until the inflammation has been alleviated.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood a second time, then let him bleed in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins on the arm are bled instead of the main vein because they are composite.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the cauterization is that the patient puts their hand in hot water until the flesh becomes red; then it must be tied moderately so that the vein appears well; then let it cool now through the skin, neither long nor wide; and the holes should be large, and the cauterization should be made close to the joint of the hand, and if pus cannot come out, put the hand in hot water again, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is winter, do not put the hand in hot water again, for one puts more cold in winter than in summer; and the cauterization of this vein is safer than all other veins.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The cauterization of the salivary gland of the right hand is worth all the diseases of the liver; and this is the manner: strain the hand and put it in hot water until the vein appears, if one can see it; and if the cauterization goes through and you cut into everything completely, nothing will hurt; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are all exposed under a layer of skin, and then put the hand in hot water again, if the pus is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn blood as much as is needed, then put oil and thread on the vein to close it quickly, and do this with each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding on the left hand is worth it for the disease of melancholy, and do everything in the same way as I told you to do with the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of the sophene is worth for all diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its salve is that the patient dips his foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein so long as it burns, and ties above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot they go many streams; therefore heal the one more swollen vein, or at the ankle, which seems worth.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed above the foot, then be careful of the nerves that are underneath, and make sure to cut across in bleeding, so that the flesh is not split.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot back in the water and let it drain completely from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the salve fails the first time, then repeat it the second time above a pot, for the place is salty; and do not doubt of nerve, as we have said, and thus make of the sophene from the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the knee's back, and its bleeding is worth it for the pain in the groin, when it's bloody hot.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	The quality of his sickness is such that the patient must enter into a bath and rinse above the ankle four times while twisting, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then let him bleed in all the ways you can, and crossing over; and be sure to bind it, for the place is clean, and it is much repented by many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then bleed any vein that opens behind the heel and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and make so much bleeding with blood as you see, and then loosen the bandage, and put on cotton and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	bleedings by cupping glass (or possibly "of a cup")
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Venetian treacles are made of horn, or metal, or glass; and venesection is done in two ways: either by cutting to attract blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping glass treatment which is not painful if done so is in two manners: or it is all hot, or slightly hot; and the cupping glass treatment that is made by piercing and extracting blood is made on fourteen points of the body, of which one is entirely under the head; and another in the neck; and two in each side of the neck; and the cupping glass under the chin; and the cupping glasses on both shoulders; and the cupping glasses above the hips; and the cupping glasses on both arms; and the cupping glasses on both legs; and the cupping glasses on both ankles; and the cupping treatment does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it is not weakened in any way, just as with a vein-bleeding treatment; and it must not be administered, nor all hot nor slightly hot, in any disease that comes from overfilling, until all of the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if due to the necessity of diseases it is necessary to bleed, or for habit, we bring each one every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and in each season; for there are such who, when they need to bleed, have a heavy head; and there are those who find repletion and ruddiness on their face, and on their head, and neck, and darkening around the eyes; and there are those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and spitting blood; and there are such who dream, and see through bloody wounds and hurt and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially if it's in the middle of the month, we will order them to bleed after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps with the inflammation of the head... that comes to the eyes, and it does not belong to be done after the evacuation of all their body; and this bleeding is in place of the cephatic sainie, and it does not belong for those who have a cold complexion to use it, or who have consumption, for it causes them great harm; and therefore it does not belong for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who bleed themselves often, become forgetful, and for this reason it's advisable to put the venetian treacle a little lower by the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The windpipe swelling in the throat is situated between the vertebrae of the neck and the rib cage, and because of this it is worth treating for constriction of the belly, and bursting of the channel of the womb, and also for a bout of indigestion; and one must push hard on it, because if it holds too tightly, so it causes an obstruction or swelling in the stomach and in the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The windpipe swellings on both sides of the neck are worth for the pains of the head, and the paining of the eyes, and migraine, and for strangulation, and for pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is situated between the vertebrae of the rib cage; and you must order the surgeon to express his hand in a way that he puts [it], so that he does not compress the artery, and let there be no uncontrolled flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The venesections under the chin are worth it for diseases of the mouth, and for decay of gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and they take the place of bleeding from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The venesections at the elbows are worth it for diseases that come from heat and repletion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The swellings of the sides are worth as much as three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from those large veins; and order the surgeon that he must not pierce too deeply at first, for the place is bare of flesh, and lies under nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The venetian treacle which is on the hip is worth it for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases beneath, and it's necessary that the treacle be large and made of metal, so that it can bleed well; and if it were thin, it might break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The venesections of the legs bleed openly, because they draw blood from the entire body, and are worth it for old pains in the veins, and in the kidneys, and in the bladder, and they cleanse the pustules; and they take the place of bleeding from the two saphenous veins, and from the two ankles, and however, they weaken the body after long use, and cause pallor in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the venetian treacle is that you first put it empty and then fill it with blood, place it quickly, move it equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the vein turn red and swollen, and appear the color of blood; then cut, and reapply the venesections, and pay attention to the condition of the body, because there are those who have thick flesh, and clear pores: if so, one must cut only once, and make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it's necessary to cut twice: the first time to thin out the large vein of blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it's necessary to cut a third time; and when we want to draw out some blood little by little, we can suffice with only one cut.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If we want much blood, so we often reiterate; and if the blood is thick, so we prick it to the bottom, and the ends are that the wounds be pierced suddenly, and it becomes necessary for one who has hard skin and dense, and who have strong pores, that you anoint the places of the cupping glass with opening and dissolving oil: whether it's in the evening, oil of violet, or oil of sweet almonds, or oil of cucumber seed; and if it's at night, oil of bryony, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person we are treating has tender skin and large pores, it is not necessary to put any oil on them, but they should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or water of bryony, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who are very damp, should get up with the aid of myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive superfluities should rise with old wine, or vinegar of the apple, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar things; and they must not take a poultice before bathing or in the bath itself, but after the bath for one or two hours; and they must not sleep afterwards, and it is necessary that he washes himself, when he should be pouched and when he is pouched.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And take care of those who are sick with choleric humors, and their blood is too acidic and inflamed; it is necessary that he takes cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuces in vinegar, and similar things; and young pigeons, and kid's flesh, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, he should take honey syrup, and aromatic wine of medium age, which is between old and new, and young pigeon meat, and young pigeons and small birds and chickens; and the day when he will be pouched, he must drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men a time a treacle or musk in front of or after the poultice, to comfort the main members; and let the blood be tempered, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The bleeding cups that are placed without hurting are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the groin and the hips, for these members do not suffer harm when the cup is placed on them, and this is done only to draw blood from one member to another, just as we put cups on the breast when there is a hemorrhage; in order to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just as we put bleeding cups on the belly and on the groin to reduce the member; and to remove pain when there is an ulcer or stone, it removes the ulcer by its attractive power by chance, or dislodges the stone from its place; and thus it acts when it is placed on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained humidity, and these bleeding cups are administered empty so that they suck only once; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with hot vinegar, just as in the diseases of the eyes; and in this way one fills the cup with warm vinegar or water in which herbs have been cooked according to medical practice.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the venetian treacle administered with fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	The instrument should be two palms in length and a half palm in depth, and on the side, around the middle, there should be a small perforation, as if to hold a needle; and it should be made of brass, soft in front so that it does not wound the patient when placing it on the limb. And in the middle, there should be a cross-shaped iron or brass rod to place a candle in the clamp, and they should be large and small according to the illnesses and age of those who take them; for the ventouses of children are different from those of the old, and the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus you should place this poultice on the limb: take a candle made of wax or flax oil, and put it in the middle of the ventouse through the rod which is inside the ventouse, so that the light is at the bottom of the ventouse so that it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and the ventouse should be over the perforation which we have said, so that when you want to, the vapour will come out, and take off the poultice; and take the flax oil as before, and repeat it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	With the cupping glass in this disease of pleurisy, very sharp, has no handle nor pipe, and is not brought unless it is full of water, and is placed on the member so alone; and that is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without cups are not brought unless to members where one cannot put cups because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and to bare flesh wounds, such as boils or nevi, and others similar; and the quality of the ulcer is that when you find ulcers in sweet clear water for puncture, take them; and dip them once in sweet clear water until they are lukewarm and have nothing inside; and then let them be cleaned with vein and cupping glass, then rub the member so it becomes red, and put on the cups; and when they are full and swollen, if that is a place where one can put cups, then put them, for that helps much afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then remove the seat of ease first, and then with vinegar, well, and then press it; and if the wound heals too late for the bloodletting, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and put on it, until the blood is congealed; and if there are many wounds, put on vitriol pounded, or gall, and similar things, until they are congealed; or you put on the seat of half-cooked broad beans, and leave them until they adhere to the wound, which will now stop it; and if you need more bloodletting, take other bloodlettings.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the bloodlettings do not want to take, then rub the wound with fresh blood, or you insert a needle until the blood comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will adhere; and when you see that they are bleeding, then powder over a small amount of alum and powdered silk, or ashes, so they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is very often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is a remedy for breakage and swelling.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know well, dear son, that foolish men flee from this chapter, for they have never seen any of the old books nor read a letter about it; and because of this reason is the science estranged in our land, for I never found any good; and I know nothing except by the science of the ancient books which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and abridged it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are prepared, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore fitting that we now say the prologue of this book, which contains the summaries of words and chapters where the wise person puts their understanding, and remains on virtue, so that those who are proven know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a break or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, it is necessary for you to hasten in treating the patient first on one side and then the other, unless something else hinders you, such as weakness of body, old age, or coldness; or if the time is not very hot, or too cold; and apply cool choleric dishes, that is to say, chilled jellies, and meat of hare and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any greasy meats, and do not fill the veins with blood so much that you have doubt of a hot abscess, or the spreading of matter in the member; if the patient's health revives at your early management which they have used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the sick person with meats that make a thick and viscous flesh, such as bread cooked in water, and rice, and cheeses, and pieces of beef, and veal belly, and onions, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment the flesh will knit together more quickly and the break will heal sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And you should know that the broken bones of old men and decrepit people cannot be well regained or soldered according to their nature because of the heat of the limbs, nor those who are too tender, such as bones of small children; but do not worry, scrape on the cracked bone large splinters which have been dried and joined the member together, so that it becomes strong again like before. And do not leave him entirely out of your work, and because of this he must be nourished with thick meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that broken bones are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is different from the break of the back, or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways that a bone can be broken.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that go across the joint, and others that are oblique, such as the break of a quill's nib for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is also a break with a cut, and a break with a small slit in it all at once.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And to each manner has its instrument and proper tool in the restoration, according to what comes back into its place; and it is known that the break of the bone by what the joint is twisted, and appears well from outside, and sounds with pressure on the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound at the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break; but it can very well have twisting, or a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you should not move the hand, but rather apply medicine that comes later, and then immobilize it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the breakage that goes in the armpit, and are the two parts disjoined, they must now be set to a point equally, so that boils hot come; and if hot boils come, then leave them alone for a day, until the boil is appeased; then set it straight to a movement that you can lightly and safely make, and know that the restoration of the joint is more easy than the restorations of those where there are pieces; then bind it, as is fitting afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, and it is stretched of two parts, then if it is an arm or a leg, or to your hand it is a small member, or with two cords, or one cord and to your hand; and set the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are disjoined, then reunite by all means the additions in their places at the movement you can, and keep that through your work does not come to the patient injury or pain; and join well the two joints of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel with your hand if it seems to you that it is not well done: then straighten it beautifully, and do not immobilize it too much, nor press as those who bring about warm apostemes and contractions in the member do, as we have warned many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is fixed in place, then chastise the patient so that they do not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other manner; and take good care that the limb be so secure that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when they feel no pain, it is not yet fixed in place, and you must put them in such a condition that they feel no pain; and take good care that it be set straight, so that twisting does not occur when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is as I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in size and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar ones: it is necessary to bandage with cloth of soft and subtle linen; and those that are large, such as thighs and shins: it is necessary to bind with a thick and strong cord, because the wide cords encompass the whole large limb and hold it evenly from all sides, so that there is no looseness; then tie light poultices around, three or four turns according to the limb, and hold your hand on a stick at one end of the cord, then go up above the break and hold it slightly less tight than before, so that the break will be separated by a little more; and soften the cord gradually and gradually until you take a great part of the true place, then take another cord, and tie around again in the same way above the broken place; then go back to the lower part of the break and hold it moderately, not too tight or too loose, as we have said in the first chapter above; then put cloth or linen compresses between the cords so that they are entirely even, then tie everything with a headband on top, and then put your well-made splints on, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or abscess, then place a soothing poultice over the abscess hot, and that which draws out the swelling, and let it be thus for some days; then bind on to the eyes with stars, and they should be of half the length of a large linen strip sewn together, or of wood from which we make cleavers, or of palm fronds, and they should be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the star that one places over the break be a bit thicker and wider than the others; and it should be as long as it needs to fit the member of smallness or largeness; then bind on the stars just as you have done in the first treatment, then tie above a thread gradually, just like in the first treatment over the break; the tighter it is up there, the more so; and it must be that the threads are medium, not too thick nor too thin, and they should be of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, such as I have seen the foolish ones who make their ligatures from twisted flax cords, and that is great error, because the bandage cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it must not have between each star less than two fingers' breadth.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is cut by the edges of the pads after they have been applied in their place, then put linen or torn cloth under them so that it does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the break and the sinew is broken, I will tell you the treatment later. (This seems to be a transition to a new topic or section in the text)
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to bind with pads all broken members at first.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Car when the limbs are large, it is not necessary to apply these poultices too soon, after 5 days or 7, or more according to your caution regarding a hot abscess; and behold here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and it is that you take flour that remains at the walls of the mill, and mix with plenty of egg, and put this concoction, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring a break to many dispositions, and especially to women and to small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster restoring breaks, dislocations, and twists: take 3 parts of absinthe, ladanium, myrrh, and aloe wood, ana .x. (parts), and add 5 parts of mirre, ana .v., and 8 parts of aloes, ana .viiij., make it into powder, and mix with abundant egg yolk; if the complexion is hot, use this plaster, because it has good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of plaster that is good for torsion: take mugwort and wormwood, an equal part; myrrh and aloes, nine parts; aloe, six parts; Armenian balm, ten parts, and grind well, and mix with water or plenty of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another manner of applying poultice to joints and loose bones out of their place, and soothing the pain happening, and the breaking of bone, they use linseed oil: take new flax, and moist it in ashes and cooked oil, and put on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This poultice does not restore, but it is good for soothing hot abscesses and properly relieving pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that restores broken bones: take dried leaves of fig tree and ground ivy (also known as "pavol terrestr" in old French), grind them together and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of applying poultice to the restoration of the breaking of bone and to reduce the remaining part of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of wormwood, camomile, violet flowers, and wheat flour, each one part; and grind, and mix with vinegar, and if the member is heated, mix it with moisted water of coriander or water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner of ointment stronger than the first, when a hardened abscess comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of balm, and seeds of flax, ointment, melilot, and hyssop, and flowers of violets and chamomile, from each a part; and crush, and boil with vinegar of salt, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that one should not put anything on the broken member to restore it except for a wax made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two temperatures, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on the broken member things that are a little bit warm and dry, such as myrrh, aloes, incense, and similar substances, which we have already mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plaster that is good for lesions and pain: take mugwort, threads from the tail of a castrated man or goose feathers, and vervain, all in equal parts, grind them together and make a plaster to bind it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove the bandage after a while, and be careful if the patient feels no pain, or if the bone has not returned to its place, do not remove it for seven days. And if pain comes to the place, or pruritus, without rest, or swells, hurry up, and loosen, and remove the ointment now; and take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and plunge in water, and lift the place, so that the pruritus ceases, and the pain is calmed. Then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, dampened in water or rosed oil, and tie up with a knot, until you are sure of hot abscess; and calm the inflammation of the member, and be rid of the pain, then resume the subtle binding, and a little ointment, and do not strain it so hard as before; and bind subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot swelling and redness and pain and inflammation have been completely removed, and you need plaster and cloth bandages again, then repeat it, just as you did the first time in the same manner.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If it does not come to the member anything of what we have said, then do not untie it until after three days or four or five or seven; and leave it twenty days at most, according to what is seen, so long as the swelling subsides, and approaches the skin above; then the restraint tightens more than before, and the flesh thickens, just as I said before; and if you see the place drying out more than necessary, know that suppuration will not come; therefore apply hot water to it, every time you untie it, and add a little wine at each tie; by this work then the swelling is cut off from the member, and quickly corrects what the foolish surgeon does, who leaves the member twisted: this is bad, and is fearful work, and I see nothing else but to let it alone and do it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	It looks like we've reached the end of the text. The author seems to be concluding by highlighting the different ways in which breaks (or fractures) can occur.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many manners of fractures are, and diverse figures, and the causes are appointed; for there are fractures that are made by percussion with a sword, and the arm breaks all the bone down to the syphilis who is under the bone, just as does a hammer or axe; and therefore it is called this manner of fracture "hammering".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone above so as to pierce it, and is called this manner of breaking "absolute"; and the wound of these two breakings is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an enclosed percussion, or fracture, or breaking of the elbow by stone, or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing break, which approaches just to the membrane that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is either great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that is healed in the bone as finely as a hair, and it is a small crack, and therefore it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made either by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by something similar, and it makes the piece of the bone enter downwards, and the hole is split like a coppersmith when they heat up over their cauldrons, so that the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often in people who have soft bones, such as the head of an infant; and it occurs in all these manners of fracture where small pieces are detached like that; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we are familiar with all manners of breaks by their appearance on them, and the investigation that has been done, and through the corrupted flesh that is on it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubs it gently with a cloth, if the break shows black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a break, take note of the patient's adverse conditions, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting blood, loss of understanding, swelling, bruising, fever ague, or the like to appear, and all this with a sure and certain sign, then he cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no alarming accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when winter comes first to you, and it's in winter, then you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon that you can see.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone is corrupted, and come the accidents which we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the breakage of the bone comes right up to the cloth that covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to cut through the broken part in this way: and it is that you take hold of the patient's head injured, and uncover on the bone in every manner that you can, and above the shape of the wound as soft as you can, and if the decormentation of blood comes to uncover the bone, or a hot abscess, then lend aid with what is necessary, and it is that you fill in the place with dampened cloths in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the hot abscess is calmed, and be assured of the decormentation of blood; then begin around the bone to remove, and this is done in two manners of work: one manner is that you cut through the narrow cutting before, and it is the form
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I insert another cutting, larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have various types of stitches, some thick and others wide, and pointed, and made of iron wire; and work lightly, so as not to cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, then it's necessary that you pierce around it, so that you can administer stitches with awls, but not too deep that they penetrate through the thin part of the bone on top; and should have above the point a margin or one circle, so that the point doesn't pass through the bone; and you'll need to have several, so that each one goes back into its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you have awls for all bones; and this is the shape of the three kinds of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place one awl above the bone and turn it back and forth until you know the bone has been pierced; then put the awl elsewhere a little further along, and so do everything around, then clip with the scissors the thickness of the bone between the punctures, and make this as subtle and lightly as you can, just as we said, so that you draw the bone out into your hand, or into any of the instruments that you have such as forceps, tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and threaded the bone, it is necessary that you reset the fragment which remains from the bone with all other instruments similar to an incisor, but it must be more sharp and subtle than the other incisors; and if anything of the small bones or scabs remain, take hold of the bone with the instruments then treat the wound with tentatives and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of doing it, which Galen says is more suitable; and the wound becomes very firm, and that's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, at the place where the break is most open; and once you have uncovered that part, then you will place under the point of this lancet-shaped instrument, which has the following shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut at one side, and if the part is sharp on both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you touch the bone all around lightly, and take good care of the cloth that is below; if it is stuck to the bone, then remove it lightly, for one removes it without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate down to the skin, and the bone is struck so only above it, and there are small pieces, then you should cover that asperity, and remove the scales with a fine rasp which you should have various quantities of, in order to smooth them out in each place where it is most convenient, according to the operation and shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you present yourself in front of coarse rasps, and then finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In every other delicate cut and subtle break, you should smooth it out according to its direction; and this is something that is not easily done by one who has put their study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the abscess is uncovered, then it is necessary that you take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound and moisten it in rose oil, and put it over the wound; then take another doubled linen cloth or two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and put it on top of the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so that you do not irritate the abscess, then administer above the other bandage and do not strain it too much until it covers the wound only; and let it be like this for one day or two, until the abscess has been pacified, then remove it and administer medicines such as lily roots, veal flour, incense powder, and aristologe, and similar things; and make powder of these things and put it on the wound, and then administer medicinal treatments without biting; and beware that the wound is completely clean before leaving any ointment or letting the edge of the cloth become attached to the brain, for when the edge of the cloth attaches itself to the brain's membrane, it festers and becomes inflamed, and the patient suffers great harm; for when something astringent is put over the abscess, it turns black on top.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, for if any bad accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no worse comes from it than the medicine that we have placed on it, which has such a virtue, then you must take part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and mix one draught in it; then apply the salve to the wound.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one is broken alone by itself, because these are two bones; and the one underneath is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it is crushed or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must press with your little finger or a small instrument on the nape, and insert equally that break inside to your index finger, and at the back part further down, until the neck returns to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.
