And if the break is in the part above the nose, and cannot be brought back into place with the thumb, then it is necessary that you put a small bandage or cloth on the head of a small rod, and use it to gently push the bone back into place.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, then do it in the same way, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can; but if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the swelling has abated, then press with your head on the nape using a cloth made of linen, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you can bind another cloth on the other side if the break is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill up the nostrils of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said a certain physician that one must moisten the tents with marrow, and move each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is well, but it must be moistened with the concoction of almond milk and egg, and mill powder; then leave the tent, as long as the bone is hard, and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes we bind onions or goose feathers to the nose instead of bandages, and if you cover it with a soft cloth and keep the break in place, and the patient blows air through and feels some relief, then do what seems best to you.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if swelling comes to the nose while you are working on it, then I put cerot or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a small amount of aqua lum, to calm it down.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess is not going away, then apply plaster outside of it with sesame flour and incense powder, mixed with almond milk, then put on light embers, and do not tie up too tightly; and if the break in the bone is small, and it has broken into small pieces, then take out the fragments with suitable instruments, then sew the wound, and cure things that cause bad flesh, and soldering, as with plasters and ointments suitable for this; and if there is no inner wound in the bone, then treat with tents, and put on poultices, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Here are some additional notes on the treatment of a broken jaw (mandible):
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is broken below and there is no wound on it, and the breakage is above only, and is not split in two, but rather curved inside, then one can tell by looking at it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the breakage is in the right part, that you insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the breakage is on the left mandible, then insert your index finger from the right hand, and push the breakage inside lightly, and pull it out with the other hand by force, and set it back in place.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the breakage of the lower jaw is split in two, it is necessary that you administer traction on both sides until it becomes equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the displacement of the teeth has occurred or bruising, then you should bind it with one thread of gold or silver or silk, and place over the broken jaw a cloth, and on top put a great needle well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and tie it up so that you can see it, and command the patient to rest, and feed him light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the patient's condition is changing, then untie it on the third day, and then put back in place what was changed, and apply a poultice over it of flour powder with plenty of egg or barley flour after you have removed the cloth; and put on top a light linen cloth, and if the poultice becomes hard and the patient's condition does not change, leave it as long as it takes to heal; many times a healing occurs in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if pus forms, administer what we have said many times. (This suggests that the treatment for pus or abscess formation is to repeat a previously mentioned remedy, possibly involving applying a poultice or dressing to draw out the infection.)
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, repair no part of the bone that has been removed; if subtle to remove with suitable instruments for it.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then you should enlarge it with fire as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is none left, then sew the wound, if it is wide, and put on one suitable ointment to stop pus, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of great strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strong forcelet breaks more than once in front, near the shoulder, and the break is either broken and separated into two, with pieces, and it is the most lightweight to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is like this when the break is without wound: that you have two assistants, so that one holds the aid that feels the forcelet broken; and the other stretches out the arm towards the part; then place equally the break on your hands, so that the form be such as it should be, and there be no appearance or crookedness.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch it further, place under the patient's shoulder a round stick of cloth or linen, and let it be as thick as needed; then pull and lift up the forcelet, and hold the stick with your hand, so that you put equally the break, just as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the end of the forcelet out because it comes from in front, it is suitable that the patient lies on his back on a mattress, and places under the shoulder a medium-sized bolster, and pushes the assistants' elbow down, so that the bone of the forcelet is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then place the break on your hands, and if it is too crowded, it is suitable that you cut in; and pull out the light pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, then cut with one of the scissors that you have; but put under the forcelet this instrument to protect the flesh.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It seems a spoon, and is not cheeked, and be as large as it ought to be, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two joints, so you see, and one is wide, and the other is narrow, such as the incision of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, count the days, and if the incision is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, apply the dressing of linen and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess forms, sooth it with a poultice made of oil, rose, and vinegar, and apply it to the skin.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is senseless from wounds and incision, is that you put powder of flour and egg whites on the bone, and put light bandages on top, and then take a very wide strip of one hand's breadth, then put double linen over the bandages and plaster; then take a slender rod three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the strip so that the ends of the strip are hanging down; and put the rod on the breakage, and turn the strip over the back healthy, and under the broken shoulder, and under the sick shoulder; and tighten each part, and when you see that the bond holds the breakage correctly, and you clearly see that the rod does not move above the broken bone, so reward it every day, and when the bindings loosen, then restrain them; and make the patient sit on his back, and put a small pillow under the shoulder, in order to lift the joint high; thus it will ease the break of the humerus by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it if any bad event happens until twenty days; then reapply the plaster, if you see that it is necessary, and tighten and leave it so, until it is restored; and it is restored at most in 28 days, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	The break of the shoulder. It seems this text is a medical guide or recipe from medieval times, specifically dealing with setting broken bones. The language and style are consistent with Old French texts from that era.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder blade breaks or becomes detached from its place and is not known to be such by touch; if it presents itself according to the figure of the breakage, and is reset according to its natural form, in all ways that you can; then put on the place powder from the mill with an abundance of egg white, and light bandages, and lay a double cloth over it. Then put on a wide and subtle bandage, one step larger than the shoulder, and under the bandage are threads in any place of the shoulder, so that you cover the whole length of the bandages with linen, so that the bandage stays evenly; and then bind it tightly with a strong bandage, so that the bandage does not move from its place, and observe the binding each day; and every time it loosens, bind it again, and put the bandage back in its place if it has gotten out of place, and lay the patient on their side. The shoulder blade is restored in twenty or twenty-five days. And when this number is completed, then release it, and be assured, for it's not bone that sets itself free lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is protruding and pointing towards the skin, then take it up, and trim it, and do what we have said in the break of the shoulder to calm down the hot swelling. (Note: "ostee" means to cut or trim something, similar to how you would trim splinters or rough edges)
de la brisure dou pis	The break of the thigh. It seems this medieval medical guide is providing instructions for setting various types of broken bones, and now it's dealing with a more serious injury like a femur fracture (break of the thigh). The text is likely describing a complex and potentially painful process that requires careful attention to detail.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it breaks often at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it turns downward, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks strength, and soon becomes feverish, and by chance may vomit blood, and the swelling appears in the broken bone, and he knows well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	The patient lies on their back and the physician places a cushion between the shoulders. Then they press the shoulders together, and assemble the two halves of the ribcage with their hands, subtly making them equal in all ways until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply plasters and bandages over the affected area subtle with salt or another light wood, and wrap it in a cloth, securing it to the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the string around to the back and strain it gently. And every hour loosen the string, and if it remains loose, tighten it again. And if it is necessary to untie it due to corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, hasten and untie it, and remove the plaster and treat what has come forth with the remedies of cures; then loosen the plaster and strain it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	The breaking of the ribs.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	It is known that the breaking of the ribs does not occur except in thick areas after the back, and at the top inside, and they do not bend unless because they are slippery; and one feels it well by examination with the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you put it even with the breakage, as it is fitting.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply a poultice and bind it with a splint if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is declining inside, the patient feels great pain and puncture, similar to that of pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; and they feel sharp pains, heat and vomit a great amount of bloody fluid. This is a serious condition, and in the past, doctors have used great remedies for it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And they say that one should administer foods that inflate the belly, in order to push the break back out.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make those, so hot abscesses will not come, if they have not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, let the doctor look at it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said to one of us that we apply cupping glasses on the place in order to suck out the fluid, and it seems to be a good reason; nonetheless, there is doubt if the cupping glass does not bring superfluous fluids to the place because of the weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said to one of us that we should cover the place with damp wool in hot oil and put tents between the ribs so that equal warmth is given all around it, then be cured with a cure of poultice, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure because of the bone that pokes through the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken ribcage, and you must put something under the instrument to protect the flesh; and then one must cut into the bone, and draw lightly, and then sew up the two edges of the wound if it is large, and heal them with poultices until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If swellings from abscesses come, put on damp cloths soaked in rose oil and apply them to the place; and treat the site of the abscess while it is still inflamed and swollen, with ointment applied to the surrounding area where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	Of the breaking of the neck (or possibly "of the break in the neck").
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	At times comes a breaking or fracture of the bone of the neck, and often it bends; and also to the spine of the back.

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the breaking of the forearm (or possibly "of a sprain in the wrist").

de la brisure du bras	The break of the arm.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", one of which is small, and that is the one that touches the shoulder; and the other is large, and that is the one that is under it, towards the small joint; perhaps only the large bone breaks, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restorations are easy, and the healings; and when the large ones are broken, then the healing is bad, and more grievous than when they were broken all at once together.

de la brisure de la main	The text appears to be a medical treatise on the treatment of arm fractures, specifically focusing on the application of bandages, splints, and other remedies to promote healing.
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and near the knuckles there are many breaks, and it only rains many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or swollen, it should be that the patient sits cross-legged and sits straight in front of himself also; then places his hand on the extended table, and extends the broken bones, and puts them back into place with the mirror, until they are well jointed; and applies a poultice and bandages, if a swelling comes, then he applies an splint according to the extent of the injury; and should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient. Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the outside, it should be that you put a splint above, and another one underneath in the palm, so that the hand may be open and straight, then tie up entirely around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the knuckles.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit. de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken cystone.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz. Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his back, then stretches each of his attendants' thread or string to an equal part, and it is when the breakage is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the thigh, so that one of the tendons inclines towards the elbow, and the other tendons are under the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the knee, and then one tendon will be near the knee, and the other will extend downwards; then place the mirrors on the bone with both hands so that it is in its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and tie it, so that an abscess does not form there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot swelling, let it subside then return to your work and treatment; the bandaging is done in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap above the break with a strong doubled bandage in two or three layers, and keep the superfluous parts out; then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the knee, and pass a long thread between the thigh and the leg, from below, and let the head of the thread come up; then turn back on the leg and on the thigh the bandage, then place on the break some stitches, and put one stitch above the bone of the leg; then fill in the space between the leg and the thigh with soft fabric to keep the pressure even, then begin to tie tightly three or four threads above the break; and as you go higher up from the break, and less tight it becomes; then take the two ends of the thread that you passed between the leg and the thigh, and tie three stitches on top, then go back down to the head of the thread, so that you come below the foot; and keep it so, if there is no movement or abscess or swelling or other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it swells again, then untie and address the swelling, as we have said many times before; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, then it is necessary to saw them off if possible; and if not possible, then it is necessary to cut through the place and draw out the splintered part; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And at no time is the tendon broken when this is done to the arm and shoulder; however, in the restoration made in this way the patient does not sound.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the tendon is restored in 7 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the various constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the joint of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there is often a small breakage, but it folds many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, then it is only a small fissure or perforation, and there are all kinds of wounds, internal and external, and everyone knows this.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one puts back what was torn to its proper place, as long as it can be moved in its place, then put on the splint, and I put a rounded stake there, if you need one, and tighten it as needed, then cover all the breakages with the other bandages, just like for an abscess and similar appearance; and apply to each accident that which is fitting until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by the name "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and it has all kinds of breakage like when it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is done similarly as with the arm; and the work is all the same. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns around in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone (fibula) is broken, then twist it in front. (This suggests a specific technique for realigning and stabilizing the fibula fracture)
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the big bone is broken, then one feels great pain, and it can be seen clearly; and it turns downward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply an extension and put it even, and tie the splints equally; but nevertheless, it is necessary if the breakage is ugly and there are many pieces that the extension be shorter and lighter; and lift according to your power.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, then take two strips of fine wood that encircle the leg from one side and the other, and are as long as the leg from the knee to below; then wrap them in two loops with a bandage above and below, and tie them together in the middle, and at this point the leg cannot lean to the right or left, and thus it is well. And some people apply one strip of wood as long as the leg, and of wood, and put the leg on to prevent movement, and properly done is what is applied in the break where there was a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or other accident; then cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but the bones of the foot sometimes break and become crooked, and you have to pay attention to several dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break in the two bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlap each other, then place the patient's foot on the ground, as if they wanted to walk, and then place your own foot over theirs, where the bones are raised, and press them until they return to their places; then apply the plaster and bandages on top, and place a small pad under the sole of the foot two fingers deep, then bind it securely, then that you have wrapped the foot with cloth, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four will have passed, you should loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether they were broken, or had been dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the toes broken, you should restore them, as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place on the broken toe a splint according to its length and a little thicker, then place under the foot that pad which I mentioned, and bind it securely; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, you should put over each toe a splint according to its size, wrapped in one piece of linen cloth, and bind the pad under the foot; and so long as the end of the pad is above the belly of the foot, you should press it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And be sure not to forget the other things that I have said for other fractures, which we have mentioned; and take care of each injury according to what is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	The breaking of the bone in the joint
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, so make her sit up and enlarge herself, then incline her to the back part of the back, and hold it from behind; then fill the natural opening of the patient with cotton, and put in as much as the size of it too; then take down the woman, and lift up the back slowly, and then the cotton will jump out, so that it comes to the entrance of nature, and returns the bone with its place; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and thus do it for VII days or around: so the break will be restored, and you see, take a bladder of thistle, and tie a cord to the anus, and put all the bladder in the natural opening; then blow into the cord strongly, until the bladder is inflated inside: nature will return the break; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the elbow or the woman's is broken, restore it thus as we have said in the hand bone; and these nearby fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and use into it and reads my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For a break signifies the right way of restoration in many dispositions; therefore listen then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the penis is broken, take a goose's gizzard and put it inside the penis; then wrap cloth around it and leave it for three days or about that long, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Je comprends mieux maintenant !
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a break with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be sutured now; so that the sutures that we have said will bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but it is left with vitriol scarring, and you have nothing else to do, then start again to restore the breakage at that same hour, or on that same day, before gangrene comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if gangrene comes, then leave the restoration just until the ninth day, as long as the gangrene is calmed down, and don't touch it on the third day or the fourth, for you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the outer layer of the skin visible, it is necessary that you put it to a light point with your hands, at an extension of little distance.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not convenient for you to put equally at your hands, then take hold of this instrument which is made of iron, which has 7 or 8 inches in length, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound; and therefore it is necessary that the maker takes 3 or 4, according as he may need them for each cure of a breakage; and let it be rounded at one end, quite large, so that it does not bend with compression on the member at your work, and have an edge in front, and be thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "splint", why the curved piece should be placed on top of the visible bone; and tie it once, so long as it recovers, and let them be equal one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle, and the instrument cannot well grasp the bone, then you should cut off the top of the bone, so that the instrument may take hold.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, with a suitable instrument, such as an awl or scraper, to your power; then remove from the bone those which are remaining in it of sharpness and small scabs.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So it is made so that he is in his place, then soak the cloth in black vinegar and properly put him in order; and do not put cerote or another thing on the wound where there is oil, lest it bring forth corruption and decay; then administer ointments when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the bandage all around according to the size of the wound, and be well warned that the wound is not bound with the fracture; and many times this has been done by foolish doctors, and death or corruption has arisen on the patient at least once; and the straining is more gentle and softer than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is foul or great, and you doubt that some evil accident will come of it, as we have said, and you find pain at the place, then do not put on ointments; but envelop around, in place of ointments, hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two that the bowstring is growing into the wound, then take out what you have put on top of all wine, and apply a healing salve for wounds, such as tetraformula ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and at vespers, as long as it remains stitched and unhealed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the member be wrapped in such a way that the bow (or bandage) lies slightly lower than the leg.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the wound does not heal after many days and it cannot be stitched up again, but rather the bow must be reapplied, know that there are small pieces of bone within it, for which reason you should probe the wound with a tent (or a probe), and remove all these loose fragments that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it, according to what he says in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and appears above the member, such as the femur or shoulder blade, and other similar bones of the large members, then do not draw it out, for many times death comes from it, but let it alone until it starts to rot; by chance it will fall out after twenty days or thirty, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	bruises that come on top of the swelling (or inflammation)
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Bruises often come after the healing of the breakage, especially when it is near the joint, and it's a sad thing to see the shape of the member; and perhaps the limb will not be able to perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then take care if the swelling is fresh: if the administering of stiptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, aloe juice, and similar others, so that you take any one of these things or all together, and mix them with stiptic vinegar or with egg whites or with oil; and apply them to the swelling in compresses, and press it well, and do not remove it for many days; then release it, and reapply another one, as long as the nodules are removed; or you strain on a piece of linen cloth made well; for the property of the linen is that it removes all the excess fluids above the members. And if the nodulation has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cover it with a plaster, and let the superfluousness become apparent; or you may apply it to any poultice-maker, until it is removed, and treat it as long as it is cured.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after healing.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breakage of the bone is restored, and after the member remains weak and delicate, it happens for many reasons: first, because it was tied too tightly, and not tied as it should be; or because there were too many ligatures, and the swelling could not come to the member; or because of a multitude of annoyances; or because of too great movements, not at its proper hour; or because it has little blood in its body, thus it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make food for the sick person, and make the body soft, so that the blood may multiply in them; and administer baths to them, and give them joy and comfort. Then put poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts a great swelling, and sometimes anoint with hot water, as long as the swelling comes to the member; and restore it to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	A double member twisted after health (or wellness)
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after its restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the shape of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the fools who say that you should break the limb all over again, and many foolish men have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and comes to great harm, and perhaps death; however, if the dislocations and tortures are fresh, then it is necessary that they be set right with hot water, or softening herbs cooked, such as leaves of marshmallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make i.e. a mollifying plaster, such as diachylon well made, and take the sap of marshmallow, and mix it with goose fat or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top; or take fatty figs, and grind them with flaxseed, and similar medicines that ease the stiffness.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the swelling is removed by constant and lengthy stroking with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And you must move the limb each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is hardened and become as hard as flint, and needs to be taken out with iron, then it is necessary to cover just up to the bone, lightly with a sharp razor, and put a compress and poultice in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, then it must be returned to its proper place immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if you delay, the swelling will grow and perhaps you will put him back in place with points; therefore do not move him to the hour that he is swollen: many times comes forth pus and other pains; however, when this happens, have the patient healed first, then leave him, until the abscess has been alleviated; then raise the member with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and cure each limb as the treatment will come back to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordained the chapters on dislocations up until this point.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Whatever happens when the jaws are dislocated in both places, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: either they are slightly out of their place, and a little softened; or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the breast, and cause saliva from the mouth that he cannot hold it, nor can close his mouth, and enwrap his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it will return to its place by itself within a few days.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, you must reset it quickly, and do not delay; and in such a way that the servants may show you the head of the patient, and put the mirror's cup in the root of the jaw dislocation within his mouth, if the dislocation is two parts; and with the other hand be outside, to put in place; and instruct the patient to loosen, his jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mirror should be placed in a straight line with it, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to return them to place, or if they are both jaws together, then warm water and oil should be applied to them, until they are lightly cleaned; and do not delay the return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient closes well with soft saliva, so put on moist cloths in a poultice made from rose oil and wax, then tie it loosely with soft strings; and the patient sleeps on his back, and his eyes should be between two cushions, so that he does not move to the right or left, nor does he try to chew, but takes light food, until the pains are removed, and the jawbones are numbed; and then eat what he wants lightly, and do not bother him with opening the mouth at eating and drinking, until the jawbone is well numbed and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be returned to their place within an hour and are not converted back to their natural position, then fever and chills set in, and possibly diarrhea, and possibly vomiting of pure yellow bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a perilous condition; and many times death comes to the person who experiences it within eight days.
de la forcelle	the jaw joint (literally "of the forceps", but in medical context referring to the mandible or jawbone)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The joint (of the mandible) cannot be dislocated from the side towards the front (i.e. into the mouth), and it can only be dislocated once towards the back, and that is when you know it has happened.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and stretches out his arms; and then presses it firmly to your palm, and it will return; then put on the plaster and bandage, and hold it in place; and the head which is towards the neck cannot dislocate itself; if not, and if it dislocates at any time, you must reset it back to its place, as we have said; then put on the plaster and bandage, and hold it in place, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; and similarly the head of the shoulder is returned when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder joint dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three manners: one of them is that it dislocates to the part below the armpit; and the second is to the part of the breast; and by chance dislocates to the top, and such things happen often; and it does not dislocate backwards for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inward for the nerves; and often dislocates downwards towards the armpit, precisely in those who have plenty of flesh, for then it springs forth suddenly; in those who have sufficient flesh, it springs at intervals, and returns to intervals.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that they have an inflammation or swelling of the shoulder, and the shoulder is swollen with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So then you should probe into it, until you are certain, and once you are sure, then start the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that a dislocation occurs when it is down towards the armpit, and makes a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find amongst them manifest differences; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and below the armpit, touching the head of the shoulder, just as if it were an ulcer; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their chest, nor move in any movements; and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it manifestly at the touch; and this manner of dislocation is not to be restored, when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister raises the patient's hand up high, then places their fingers under the collarbone, and raises the jointure with force upwards to its place; and the minister raises the hand and extends it upwards, then places it back down, and it will come back quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If it does not come as we have said in four days after that, then the patient must be bathed in hot water; and a poultice softening and soothing, as decoction of althea and fenugreek and mehillet in water, is brought and applied. Then the patient is seated on their back, and under the armpit a woolen compress equal, not too soft nor too hard, is placed. The doctor puts his foot against the compress, and lifts the head of the shoulder forcefully, and pulls the hand of the patient; and another servant takes hold of the head of the patient, so that it does not move downwards. That shoulder comes back immediately, and you see if he resets it in this way: then make sure there is a man present who is greater than the patient; and is straight towards the side, and presses their shoulder under the armpit of the patient, and lifts the arm in high, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another servant pulls the hand of the patient downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can lift with him some heavy thing, and the dislocation will come back now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And one also remedies it in another way: and this is how a long stick is stuck in the ground, so that the head of it is as thick as a fist, and not too large or too thin; then it is placed under the patient, but so that it is draped softly above, and the patient's hand holds onto the length of the wood; then his hand is extended from the other side in this way: take a stick with two arms and four inches wide, which has a head as thick as a thumb to enter into the midst of the cleft, according to this shape.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	and tie a cloth on top of the spit so that it does not hurt the patient, then place it under the patient's collarbone; and stretch out your arm over the long spit, and tie the elbow to the spit, and the arm at the hand, then put the arm on a cushion of a wooden board, one finger's width thick, and have the hands hanging down, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will come back immediately.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And once it is healed, in whatever way it may be, then you should place under the collarbone a ball of wool of equal thickness; and apply an ointment made from flour powder with incense and egg yolks all over the shoulder and around it; and bind the bandage under the collarbone gently, and turn the cloth back on the ointment, and wrap the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he rest a little while, until the members are comforted, because it will heal more quickly; and then let him rest some more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place because of moisture that has come in, or for another reason, then you must administer cauterizations at three pores, as it is shown in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and the dislocation happens again after seven days, and the joint does not hold and the arm cannot be lifted upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs towards the chest or breasts or back is caused by a blow or stretching of the hands, and it requires another type of treatment. And one must treat it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes swelling in the member and slow movement, then the patient should bathe many times until the swelling is alleviated and the member returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated in various ways and returns to its place in the same way, whether it was dislocated in front or behind, and the dislocation is not restored, because one can see it well and feel it well; and dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the cut patient with the thread, so you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to treat it so that hot abscesses do not form, because if hot abscesses do form, it will be painful to reduce it; and by chance it cannot be completely reduced, especially when it occurs in the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and by chance death can occur.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is this: when it can be reduced to such an extent that one can bring it back into place, then you should extend its hand with both of yours; and its arms should be spread out, and the hands of the minister should follow the shoulder around, on top and underneath, and push the joint into its hollow or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it will come back when it doubles its hand over its own hand, and presses the root of the palm against the shoulder that was dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it will not return to its place, administer strong extension; and let two ministers stretch the arm, and bind it with two bandages, so that it does not move at the stretching; then turn the arm from each side, then wrap a double length and wide cloth around it; and when the surgeon has joined the joint to his hand, he anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then presses the joint firmly, until it returns; and when it is back in place, put on dry ointment with egg-white, and bind it firmly, and support the arm at the neck of the patient, and let him rest for some days, then untie.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then release the bandage and let it be; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then reapply the ointment and the bandage, and let it be thus for some days, until it is firmly set, and then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.
