And if he feels pain after the joint has been reset, and it moves, then bathe and scrub him well, and press so that it is alleviated; or you put a sheep's fat on the joint, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and make him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put the fat on again, and then have him enter the bath; and thus do it twice or three times, until he is healed; and if you see fit, then put moist heated flax on him and stretch it over; so that it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand.
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated and it is a light return, more than other joints. Nevertheless, it is necessary to bring it back into place quickly, even if it is swollen or if a hot abscess forms in it.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is that you place the patient's sick hand on a table, and extend their fingers and have the assistant straighten them, so that he places his palm over the appearance of the joint, and push it until it returns to its place; however, it is necessary for you to check if it is in good place; then have the patient place the back of their hand on a table in extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is on the back of the hand, then the patient puts their back against the table, and the surgeon places their hand above the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is good If not, then bind on soothing plasters over the abscess, and let it be so without starting again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in its place after any number of days, then the joint remains twisted; and do not hurt anything more to the patient than making his hands numb, and being unable to grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves are crushed, or the arteries; for there is no other remedy except to strain by cauterizing near the case, and perchance it will be worth nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is back in place, then apply the ointment that we have said, and bind it and let it be for five days, then release it and let it be thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well and there is some swelling, then bathe the hand in warm water, and rub it gently until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	At any time the shoulder of the hand is dislocated on both sides, at any time to the back of the palm or to the belly; then hold the shoulder and bind the dislocation to your pouches until it returns, then support the head of the shoulder, and push it towards the part where it is disconnected; and let it be so for two days, and then make it equal on that day; and after that tie it as we have said, and loosen it from there, and move it, and reattach it to it; and do this often, until it is tight, and all in the same way do, if it is dislocated at the belly of the hand, and do so as you have done before, until it is healed; and do just that, when it is dislocated from the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the hip bone (ischium) at the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the hip bone (ischium) at the back or near the tailbone is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, because death quickly follows the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The signs of this are that the stools jump out without any willpower, and they cannot hold it, and many times are softened some member, or both hips or both arms, or sometimes the shin moves to four parts; and that which moves at the back is called "gibbosity": the cure is that you repair it if gibbosity came from childhood: if there is no cure nor salvation whatever.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or shocks or similar things, the old ways of cures by great words say there is not at all a great benefit; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and have fashioned instruments in various manners.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gibbosity which comes to the front of the chest, there is no cause nor health; and similarly that which comes straight on both sides, and one cannot cure those that come squarely to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient lies stretched out on his face in a straight place, and has something strained under him so he does not get hurt; then stick two tongs at the head into the earth firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a string behind the sick person's legs, and another behind the hips, and thighs, and knees; and two servants know the strings, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two tongs; and they are well fastened, the tongs as we have said, and the physician puts his hands on the spine firmly, until it revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this treatment, then take a table of three arms' length, and sharpen the under part, and have the patient sit on one side, and place the head of the table under the pimple, then put the middle of the table on the spine; and place the fingers of the mirror [or forceps] on the other end of the table, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do the same with the tourniquet that turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And take two skewers of great arm's length, and have them near the patient's feet two others, and have between each skewer, a hand's breadth of space long; and have on each skewer one notch, or the tourniquet fits in, and be the skewers firmly stuck in the earth, so that they do not move; and between the two skewers have one skewer turning, where the ligament turns, and have in the two turnings two small skewers of a hand's breadth long, to turn the tourniquet; and then tie the string which is among the pieces to the tourniquet towards the head, and the other string towards the feet to the other tourniquet, and each of the attendants turn their tourniquet to all the string, and the master set the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is equalized, then apply desiccating plaster with abundant egg, and then bandage them, and then cut the cord from a piece of wood three digits long, that it may stretch out the place of the swelling and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a ligature, as we have said, and use the patient to subtle nourishment until they are healed; and if anything comes in the end of healing, then administer softening and soothing medicines, with the cord that we mentioned before; and sometimes administer an onion, and never will the appearance come on the back spine of the back, and think you that it is dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, for which you should not have presumption: perhaps would make come death.
des dislocations de la hainche	It looks like we've reached a new section of text.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that dislocations occur only in the joints of the hip and the shoulder, but not so in other joints; and the joint of the hip is displaced according to four parts: inward and outward, front and back; and more inward, and it comes undone before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation is thus that when you join the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the diseased kneecap opens more than the healthy one, and the diseased person cannot bend their knee to the fire; and the place where there is a hot abscess swelling, because the hip bone comes into it.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him whose it comes on the outside is that this accident is contrary to those in front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of him whose it comes on the inside is that he can move his leg well according to its completion; however, do not bend his knee without pain, and if one wants to make him go, he cannot walk forward, holds back his urine, swells the groin, and when he goes, he passes above the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him whose it comes behind is that he cannot spread his knee joint, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the veins of the groin are at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this resemblance of dislocation is that you return to see if the dislocation was ancient and has remained according to its position, in which case there is no cure; and it is not necessary to have any hope.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is one of the four types of dislocation, you should hurry to return the joint to its proper place, inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and there will be no need for any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must appear the minister strong, and stand the leg strong with two hands, or on one lien that is tied above the knee; and another minister extends his hand upwards in such a way that he pushes his hands beneath his buttocks, then he tightens him with a single lien above the crotch; and another pricks the chief of the lien; and they all stretch up and down together at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to all four types of dislocations, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then it is necessary to apply treatment to its resemblance When the dislocation is at the shoulder, it is necessary that you bind the patient on their chest side, then put the lien above the root of the thigh, and the place which is beneath the elbow; then stretch the lien upwards towards the armpit, and towards the buttock; then take another minister's arms, and he must encircle the thick part of the ill-made crotch, and extend it in the back very far: it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot close it in this manner which we have said, then it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft thread over both heels and both shanks, and the sick leg be stretched out two inches more than the others; then hang it on the head of a tree, and over the ground two arms of length; then command the servant to grasp the handle of the stirrup, and another servant hanging with the patient, who grasps firmly the handle, for now the joint returns hastily.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at the farthest, then the patient lies down as we have said in one who has sciatica, and tighten the bandage over the sick leg properly, and over the knee also; then put two burning torches, one at the head and the other at the feet, then stick a burning torch between the handles for the patient in the middle of the shape; and hang moistened rags around him so he doesn't harm himself, then stretch out each servant towards him, and the barber puts an equal amount of pressure on his hand where the dislocation is.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on a table, and press him thus as we have said in the Galenism, and put the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it must be stretched hastily and according to what I have said; and place the mirror on the patient's pain above the sick joint, then press with the other hand and stretch it down towards the elbow.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it does not need to stretch the patient downwards or raise him up from the earth, but rather he should be as if his thigh were dislocated in front, as we have said concerning the sleeping on two thighs; and put him on his back, and extend the bandage such as we have said before, and must press on the joint at the table; and it will be in place when the patient stretches out his legs, and they will be equal; then join the thighs, and apply the plaster, and strain with a strip of cloth, so that the thigh does not move; and if he rests for three days or four, then loosen him, and put the plaster on; and if you see that they are equal, tie it as before, and leave him for three days; then loosen him, and let him go gently, until the member is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	On the dislocation of the elbow.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The joints are dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and do not become dislocated in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at his knee, and if it will not return to its place at the knee, know that he is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you have the patient sit upright, and stretch out his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take hold of his knee with your palms, and draw it between your arms, then bend both sides of the knee together; and another assistant stretches his foot so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he has returned his leg to his knee lightly; and apply the poultice on top, and have him keep his leg at the knee, and bind them tightly together for three days or four, then loosen it; and do not let the patient walk until the member is comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not straight, administer strong extension, just as we have said in the treatment of the hiccups, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	It seems like a new topic!
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The toes are sometimes swollen, and sometimes completely dislocated within and behind.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it bends forward to the part where it is dislocated; the return is easy, and the limb must be stretched slightly in one's hands when it is just seized.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you must have the patient sit up straight, and the attendants stretch the leg out over the ankle; then pull the foot to yourself with your right hand, and then with your left two times, then stretch it upwards, and push the foot well upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, you must repeat the procedure, because it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, you must have the patient lie on their back on the ground, and fix a firm peg in the earth between his thighs, and bind cloths around, so as not to hurt the patient; then have one attendant stretch the leg with both hands, or with a cord, over the foot itself; then each attendant stretches equally, and the peg should be right between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when you stretch it; then place the same attendant's hands on either side of the dislocation, and another attendant will take the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is placed on the point, he puts the poultice and bandages over it, and strengthens the splint, and ties the foot to the leg, and guards the tendons that are above the ankle behind, so that the bandage is not too tight; then leaves him for 2 days or 3, and if the bandage loosens, he should reapply it; then unloosens on the third day or quarter, and forbids the patient to go for 4 days; and if he goes before the time is up, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if pus or swelling comes up, you should reduce it, as we have said elsewhere, until they are completely healed.
des dois	It looks like we've reached the end of this medieval medical text! "De dislocatione pedis" (On dislocation of the foot) seems to be a brief guide for treating a specific type of injury or condition. If you'd like, I can try to summarize what we've learned from it.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated (or sore), they should be gently stretched without effort, and that's a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any part of the back of the foot, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a table completely upright, and put your foot over the part of the joint that shows, then press with your foot firmly until it returns; and when it is evened out, and nothing shows, then place under the sole of the foot a board two fingers thick, then strengthen the splint, and leave him for 3 days, then unloosen him; and make him rest, until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	It looks like we're switching to a new section of the text, which deals with treating wounds and dislocations together! This might be an interesting combination of injury types, as both wounds and dislocations require different approaches to healing. If you'd like, I can try to summarize what we've learned so far from this medieval medical text.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and you have not used it for a long time, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and slow, nor bold; and use at first soothing remedies on the hot abscess, and let the patient be in the hands of God, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the member to its place, so that the hot abscess comes; and when the member is in place, administer soothing remedies on the hot abscess, and cure the wound, as it becomes necessary, with drying ointments; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are broken, then set them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering into a way of fear, according to what I have said, for this will harm you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge to arm yourself and your body.
Amen	So be it.
